Two Conditions for the Opening Takbir: Intention and Audibility
Ruling with proof for two conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi conditions for the opening takbir (tahrrimah) and explain the proof from Quran 87:15 that requires audibility.

Core Idea
The takbir must be simultaneous with intention and audible to oneself.

This passage focuses on two essential conditions for the opening takbir (tahrrimah) that validate the prayer. First, the intention must coincide with the takbir without any delay. Second, the takbir must be pronounced audibly so that the person can hear himself. The author supports both conditions with Quranic evidence and provides a precise definition of what constitutes valid speech (natiq) in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions
Read the passage and extract the two explicit requirements: (a) the intention should not be delayed after the takbir, and (b) the takbir should be said such that the person hears himself.
The first condition was already mentioned in the rule of 'no gap' and is reiterated here.
2
Locate the proof
Find the verse cited: 'And mentions the name of his Lord and prays' (Quran 87:15). Note how it is used for both conditions.
The word 'dhikr' indicates verbal remembrance, supporting audibility.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the verse proves each condition: the sequence (mention then pray) implies simultaneity of intention and takbir; the word 'dhikr' implies utterance that can be heard.
This is a zanni dalala because the connection relies on linguistic interpretation.
4
Understand the linguistic definition
Study the definition of natiq: movement of tongue, sound, and hearing by oneself. This is the minimum standard for the takbir.
If the person next to him also hears, it is jahr (loud); otherwise it is sirr (quiet).
5
Apply to practice
Apply the condition: the takbir is valid only if the person hears himself under normal conditions. Mere thought without sound is insufficient.
This applies to all verbal acts in prayer, including quiet recitation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۳۵۲)[۹] تحریمہ کے وقت نیت ہو اس سے مؤخر نہ ہو۔ [۱۰] تحریمہ اس طرح کہے کہ خود سن لیوے ہیچ مذہب پر تشریح : یہاں دو باتیں ہیں [1] ایک یہ کہ جب نیت کرے اس کے ساتھ ہی تکبیر تحریمہ کہے، یہ بات پہلے بھی التحریمہ بلافصل، میں گزر چکی ہے، [۲] اور دوسری بات یہ ہے کہ تکبیر تحریمہ اتنی آواز سے کہے کہ خودسن لے۔ وجه : ان دونوں باتوں کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ (۱) و ذكر اسم ربه فصلی (آیت ۱۵ ، سورۃ الاعلی ۸۷ ) اس آیت میں ہے کہ نماز پڑھنے سے پہلے اللہ کا ذکر ہویعنی تکبیر ہو، جس کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ نیت کے ساتھ ہی تکبیر کہے۔ اور ذکر کا لفظ بتلارہا ہے کہ آواز سے تکبیر کہے۔ لغت : النطق : تین باتیں ہوں تو نطق ہے [1] زبان کو حرکت ہو حروف ادا ہوں [۲] پھسپھساہٹ ہو [۳] اور کان کو آواز آئے تو یہ نطق سری ہے۔ تکبیر تحریمہ، قرآت سری اور طلاق واقع ہونے کا مدار اسی پر ہے۔ اور برابر والے کو بھی یہ آواز سنائی دے تو یہ قرآت جہری ہے۔
Translation: (352) [9] The intention should be at the time of the tahrrimah, not delayed after it. [10] He should say the tahrrimah in such a way that he hears it himself. Explanation: There are two matters: [1] When he makes intention, he should immediately say the opening takbir—this has passed earlier in 'without a gap'. [2] The second is that the opening takbir should be said with a voice that he himself hears. Proof for both: The verse 'And mentions the name of his Lord and prays' (Q. 87:15) indicates that before prayer, there is dhikr (takbir) and that dhikr implies audibility. Linguistic note: 'Natiq' (speech) requires three things: [1] movement of the tongue and utterance of letters, [2] some sound (whispering), [3] hearing oneself. This is 'sirr' (quiet) recitation. The ruling for takbir tahrrimah, quiet recitation, and the occurrence of divorce depends on this. If the person next to him also hears, it is 'jahr' (loud) recitation.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage adds two further conditions related to the takbir: (1) that the intention must not be delayed after the takbir—they must be simultaneous (already covered in the previous rule of no gap), and (2) that the takbir must be audible to the person himself. The author provides the Qur'anic verse from Surah al-A'la as evidence: 'And mentions the name of his Lord and prays,' arguing that 'mentions' implies utterance. The linguistic note defines 'natiq' as speech that involves tongue movement, sound, and hearing by oneself; this is the standard for takbir and quiet recitation. If others hear it, it is considered loud recitation. The Hanafi school holds that for the takbir to be valid, one must hear himself under normal conditions; mere thought without sound is insufficient.

Key Terms
نطق (natiq): Speech that involves tongue movement, sound, and hearing by oneself; distinguishes between silent thought and audible utterance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum requirement for the opening takbir to be valid?
A) The takbir must be heard by the person offering the prayer.
B) The takbir must be heard by the imam.
C) The takbir must be said loudly.
D) The takbir must only be thought in the heart.

Key Takeaway
The opening takbir requires both simultaneous intention and audibility to oneself; mere thought is insufficient.

Follower's Intention to Follow the Imam
States that the follower must intend to follow the imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the requirement of intention for the follower and identify its consequence for the validity of congregational prayer.

Core Idea
Without intention to follow, the prayer behind an imam is invalid as jam'ah.

The simple act of standing behind an imam does not automatically make one a follower (muqtadi). The Hanafi school emphasizes that a specific intention to follow the imam is a condition (shart) for the prayer to be counted as congregational. This lesson unpacks that condition and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its category
The act under consideration is praying behind an imam (iqtida'). It falls under the ibadat category of salah.
The passage is a ruling statement: it declares a condition for validity.
2
Identify the condition (shart)
The condition is 'intention to follow the imam' (niyyat al-mutaba'ah). The follower must form this specific intention.
This condition is separate from the general intention to pray salah.
3
Apply the condition to determine validity
If the intention is present, the prayer is valid as iqtida'. If absent, the prayer is not considered following the imam.
The consequence: without intention, the prayer may be invalid as jam'ah or treated as a solitary prayer.
4
Distinguish from generic congregational intention
Mere intention to pray in congregation (jam'ah) is insufficient; one must specifically intend to follow that particular imam.
This avoids confusion with the imam's own intention.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۳۵۳) [۱۱] مقتدی کے لئے متابعت کی نیت کرنا۔ تشریح : مقتدی ہے تو امام کی متابعت کی نیت کرے گا تب اس کی اتباع میں نماز ہوگی ، ورنہ اس کی اتباع میں نماز نہیں ہوگی۔
Translation: (353) [11] For the follower, intending to follow [the imam]. Explanation: If one is a follower, he must intend to follow the imam; only then will his prayer be valid as following. Otherwise, his prayer will not be considered as following the imam.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This brief passage addresses the requirement for a person praying behind an imam (muqtadi). The follower must specifically intend to follow the imam. Without this intention, the prayer is not considered an act of following (iqtida'), and thus the prayer may be invalid or not count as congregation. The Hanafi school emphasizes that the intention of following is a condition for the validity of the follower's prayer in jam'ah.

Key Terms
متابعت (mutaba'ah): Following the imam in actions of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a person prays behind an imam without intending to follow him?
A) The prayer is valid as if he prayed alone.
B) The prayer is invalid as an act of following the imam.
C) The prayer is valid but he must repeat it.
D) The prayer is valid if he intended to pray in congregation in general.

Key Takeaway
The follower must specifically intend to follow the imam; without it, the prayer is not valid as congregational prayer.

Condition of Standing for Takbir Tahrimah
Ruling with proof on the condition of Takbir Tahrimah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of takbir tahrimah in prayer and explain the proof from the hadith.

Core Idea
Takbir tahrimah must be said while standing; saying it while bowing invalidates the prayer.

In the Hanafi school, the opening takbir (takbir tahrimah) is a fard that must be performed with specific conditions. One of the most important conditions is that it must be said while the worshiper is standing, before bending for ruku. This lesson examines the textual basis for this ruling from the matn, the supporting athar, and the hadith from Ali ibn Abi Talib. Understanding this condition ensures that the prayer is valid from its very beginning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the takbir tahrimah (opening takbir). What is its legal status? The passage states it is fard (obligatory). If forgotten, the prayer must be restarted.
Hanafi: fard; omission invalidates prayer.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith from Ali ibn Abi Talib: 'When the Messenger of Allah stood for prayer, he said the takbir.' This is found in Sunan Abi Dawud. It is a hadith ahad (zanni al-thubut).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The operative phrase 'when he stood for prayer, he said the takbir' indicates that the takbir is said in the standing posture, not while bending. The condition of standing is derived from this sequence.
The hadith does not explicitly forbid saying takbir while bowing, but the natural implication is that it is said in the standing posture.
4
State the thamarah al-khilaf
There is no valid ikhtilaf among the four schools on this fundamental point—all require the opening takbir while standing. The practical consequence is that if one says it while bowing, the prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
Some may confuse with the takbir for moving to ruku, which is different.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب) شروط الصلوة واركانها (۳۵۱) والاتيان بالتحريمة قائما قبل انحنائه للركوع (۳۵۲) و عدم تاخير النية عن التحريمة سے معلوم ہوا کہ نماز شروع کرنے کے لئے تکبیر تحریمہ کہنا فرض ہے۔ (۳) عن ابراهيم قال : اذا نسي تكبيرة الافتتاح استأنف ۔ (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۸ فی الرجل ینسی تکبیرة الافتتاح، ج اول ص ۲۱۵، نمبر ۲۴۶۵ مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب من نسی تكبيرة الافتتاح، ج ثانی ، ص ۴۶، نمبر ۲۵۴۱) اس اثر میں ہے کہ تکبیر افتتاح بھول جائے تو نماز دہرائے جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ تکبیر تحریمہ فرض ہے۔ لغت : تکبیر تحریمہ: تحریمہ باندھنے کے لئے جو اللہ اکبر کہتے ہیں، یہ تکبیر تحریمہ ہے، یہ فرض ہے ، اس کے بغیر نماز نہیں ہوگی ۔ تحریمہ باندھنا: ناف کے نیچے جو ہاتھ باندھتے ہیں اس کو تحریمہ باندھنا کہتے ہیں، یہ سنت ہے۔ رکوع: آدمی اتنا جھکے کہ ہاتھ گھٹنے پر پہنچ جائے تو یہ رکوع میں جانا ہو گیا، اب تکبیر تحریمہ جائز نہیں، اور ہاتھ ابھی گھٹنے پر نہیں پہنچ رہا ہے تو ابھی تک قیام کی حالت ہے، یہاں تک تکبیر تحریمہ کہہ سکتا ہے۔ ترجمه : (۳۵۱) تکبیر تحریمہ کھڑے کھڑے کہے رکوع میں جھکنے سے پہلے۔ الله تشریح : تکبیر تحریمہ قیام کی حالت میں کہے، اور رکوع میں جھکنے سے پہلے کہے۔ وجه : عن علي بن ابي طالب قال كان رسول الله عله الا الا اذا قام الى الصلوة كبر ۔ (ابوداؤد شریف، باب ما یستفتح به الصلوة من الدعاء، ص ۱۱۸، نمبر ۷۶۰ ) اس حدیث سے پتہ چلا کہ قیام کی حالت میں تکبیر کہے۔
Section: Conditions of prayer and its pillars. (351) And performing the tahrimah while standing before his bending for rukua. (352) And not delaying the intention from the tahrimah. It is understood from this that saying takbir tahrimah for starting prayer is obligatory. (3) From Ibrahim: 'If one forgets the opening takbir, he should restart.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, concerning the man who forgets the opening takbir, vol. 1, p. 215, no. 2465; Musannaf Abdurrazzaq, chapter on one who forgets the opening takbir, vol. 2, p. 46, no. 2541) In this athar, if one forgets the opening takbir, he should repeat the prayer, from which it is understood that takbir tahrimah is obligatory. Lexicon: Takbir tahrimah: The words 'Allahu Akbar' said for tying the tahrimah; it is obligatory; without it the prayer is not valid. Tying the tahrimah: Tying the hands below the navel is called tying the tahrimah; it is sunna. Ruku: A person bends so much that his hands reach the knees; then he has entered ruku. Now takbir tahrimah is not permissible, and if his hands have not yet reached the knees, he is still in the state of standing; he can say takbir tahrimah until then. Translation: (351) Say the takbir tahrimah while standing, before bending for ruku. Allah. Explanation: Say the takbir tahrimah in the state of standing, and before bending for ruku. Proof: From Ali ibn Abi Talib, he said: 'When the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, stood for prayer, he said the takbir.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on what to begin prayer with from supplication, p. 118, no. 760) From this hadith it is understood that the takbir is said in the state of standing.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the condition of Takbir Tahrimah in prayer. The author states that the opening takbir (takbir tahrimah) must be performed while standing, before the worshiper bends for ruku. The matn explicitly says 'while standing before his bending for ruku'. The commentary clarifies that if one forgets the takbir, the prayer must be restarted, indicating its obligatory nature. The lexical note distinguishes 'takbir tahrimah' (the words 'Allahu Akbar' for entering prayer, which is fard) from 'tahrimah bandhna' (tying the hands below the navel, which is sunna). The definition of ruku is given: bending until hands reach the knees. The takbir tahrimah is only valid before that point. The proof is a hadith from Ali ibn Abi Talib that the Prophet (salla Allahu alayhi wa sallam) used to say the takbir when he stood for prayer, establishing that it is said in the standing posture. Thus, the Hanafi ruling is clear: takbir tahrimah is a fard that must be performed while standing, before ruku.

Key Terms
تکبیر تحریمہ (takbir tahrimah): The words 'Allahu Akbar' said at the beginning of prayer to enter its state of prohibition.
قیام (qiyam): Standing posture in prayer.
رکوع (ruku): Bowing from the waist so hands reach the knees.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on saying Takbir Tahrimah while bowing (ruku)?
A) The prayer is valid if said while bowing
B) The prayer is invalid because it must be said while standing
C) It is makruh but prayer is valid
D) It is permissible if one has an excuse

Key Takeaway
Takbir tahrimah must be said while standing before ruku; doing otherwise invalidates the prayer.

Intention Not Delayed and Utterance Audible for Takbir Tahrimah
Two conditions for takbir tahrimah with Quranic proof and lexical expansion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two wajib conditions for takbir tahrimah (concurrent intention and self-audible utterance) and derive them from the Quranic proof.

Core Idea
Takbir tahrimah requires simultaneous intention and self-audible utterance – both are wajib.

The opening takbir (tahrimah) is the gateway to prayer. This passage focuses on two conditions that must be met for it to be valid: the intention (niyyah) must be present at the very moment of saying 'Allahu Akbar', and the utterance must be audible to oneself. These conditions are derived from a Quranic verse and have practical implications for every prayer.

Guided Path
1
State the two conditions
Identify the two requirements for takbir tahrimah mentioned in the passage: (1) intention not delayed from the takbir, (2) utterance audible to oneself.
2
Locate the Quranic proof
The author cites verse 87:15 of Surah al-A'la: 'And he mentions the name of his Lord and prays.' Identify how this verse is used as evidence.
3
Trace the linguistic inference
The word 'dhikr' (remembrance) implies an audible utterance. Explain how the Hanafi school connects this to the timing and audibility of the takbir.
The verse mentions remembrance before prayer; the takbir is that remembrance.
4
Define 'nattq' according to Hanafi lexicography
The passage defines nattq (elocution) as requiring three elements: tongue movement with letters, whispering (audible to self), and the sound reaching one's ear. Note that this standard applies to takbir tahrimah, silent recitation, and even divorce.
Self-audibility is the threshold for 'silent' recitation.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some schools do not require audibility for the takbir. Identify that the Hanafi position is based on this specific interpretation of the verse and is considered the stronger view (على الاصح).
The practical consequence: for a Hanafi, a purely mental takbir does not begin the prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۳۵۲)[۹] تحریمہ کے وقت نیت ہو اس سے مؤخر نہ ہو۔ [۱۰] تحریمہ اس طرح کہے کہ خود سن لیوے هېر مذهب پر تشریح : یہاں دو باتیں ہیں [1] ایک یہ کہ جب نیت کرے اس کے ساتھ ہی تکبیر تحریمہ کہے، یہ بات پہلے بھی التحریمہ بلافصل، میں گزر چکی ہے، [۲] اور دوسری بات یہ ہے کہ تکبیر تحریمہ اتنی آواز سے کہے کہ خودسن لے۔ وجه : ان دونوں باتوں کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ (۱) و ذكر اسم ربه فصلی (آیت ۱۵ ، سورۃ الاعلی ۸۷ ) اس آیت میں ہے کہ نماز پڑھنے سے پہلے اللہ کا ذکر ہویعنی تکبیر ہو، جس کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ نیت کے ساتھ ہی تکبیر کہے۔ اور ذکر کا لفظ بتلارہا ہے کہ آواز سے تکبیر کہے۔ لغت : النطق : تین باتیں ہوں تو نطق ہے [1] زبان کو حرکت ہو حروف ادا ہوں [۲] پھسپھساہٹ ہو [۳] اور کان کو آواز آئے تو یہ نطق سری ہے۔ تکبیر تحریمہ، قرآت سری اور طلاق واقع ہونے کا مدار اسی پر ہے۔ اور برابر والے کو بھی یہ آواز سنائی دے تو یہ قرآت جہری ہے۔
Translation: (352) [9] The intention should be at the time of tahrimah, not delayed after it. [10] Say the tahrimah such that he himself hears it, on every school? Explanation: Here there are two matters: [1] One is that when he intends, he should say takbir tahrimah simultaneously; this matter has already passed under 'tahrimah bilaa fasl'. [2] The second matter is that he should say takbir tahrimah with a voice such that he himself hears it. Proof: The proof for both matters is this verse: 'And he mentions the name of his Lord and prays' (Surah al-A'la, 87:15). In this verse, before praying, there is remembrance of Allah, meaning takbir; this implies that the takbir is said with the intention. And the word 'remembrance' indicates that the takbir is said with voice. Lexicon: Elocution (nattq): Elocution occurs when three things are present: [1] the tongue moves and letters are produced, [2] there is whispering, [3] and the ear hears the sound; this is silent elocution. Takbir tahrimah, silent recitation, and the occurrence of divorce depend on this. And if the person next to him also hears this sound, it is loud recitation.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on two conditions related to takbir tahrimah. First, the intention (niyyah) must not be delayed from the takbir; they must be concurrent. Second, the utterance (nattq) of the takbir must be audible to the one saying it—he must hear himself. The author notes that the first point has been covered earlier. The proof is a Quranic verse (87:15) which mentions remembering Allah before prayer; the word 'remembrance' implies an audible utterance. The lexical note defines 'nattq' (elocution) as requiring tongue movement, whispering (audible to oneself), and the sound reaching one's ear. This standard is used for silent recitation and divorce validity as well. Thus, for takbir tahrimah, one must both intend simultaneously and articulate audibly to oneself.

Key Terms
نیت (niyyah): Intention in the heart for the prayer.
نطق (nattq): Audible articulation that includes movement of tongue, whispering, and self-hearing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is required regarding the utterance of Takbir Tahrimah according to this passage?
A) It must be loud enough for others to hear
B) It must be audible to the person himself
C) It is sufficient to think it in the heart
D) It is not required at all

Key Takeaway
Takbir tahrimah must be accompanied by intention at the same moment and must be uttered audibly to oneself; both are wajib based on Quranic evidence.

beginner
6 min
Muqtadi's Intention to Follow the Imam
Obligation for a follower to intend following the imam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a muqtadi must intend to follow the imam and explain the hadith evidence that establishes this requirement.

Core Idea
A muqtadi must consciously intend to follow the imam for his prayer to be valid as congregational.

This lesson examines the requirement for a follower (muqtadi) in congregational prayer to have a specific intention of following the imam. The Hanafi school holds this as a necessary condition for the follower's prayer to be counted as validly performed in congregation. We will explore the primary hadith proofs that establish this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its subject
Determine what act is being ruled upon and what the ruling is. Here, the act is the muqtadi's intention to follow the imam, and the ruling is that this intention is necessary for the prayer to be considered following the imam.
The subject is the muqtadi, the follower in congregational prayer.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Find the main evidence cited. The primary hadith is: 'The imam is appointed only to be followed; so do not differ with him...'
Sahih al-Bukhari and Sahih Muslim report this hadith.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Examine how the hadith implies the requirement of intention. The phrase 'to be followed' indicates that following must be a conscious act; mere physical alignment without intention does not constitute true following.
The Hanafi usul principle: a command to follow implies the necessity of intent.
4
Consider the second hadith
The text also cites the hadith 'The imam is a guarantor and the mu'adhdhin is a trustee.' This reinforces that the imam has a responsibility, and the follower must submit to him with intention.
This hadith adds weight to the necessity of intention.
5
Apply the ruling
If a muqtadi lacks the intention to follow the imam, his prayer is not considered valid as a congregational prayer, though it may be valid individually.
The consequence: the follower misses the reward and rulings specific to congregation.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the requirement for a follower (muqtadi) to intend following the imam. The matn states that the follower must intend following. The commentary explains that without this intention, the prayer is not considered as following the imam. The proof is the hadith: 'The imam is appointed only to be followed,' which indicates that following must be intentional and complete. A second hadith states that the imam is a guarantor, implying the follower must submit to him, which requires intention. Thus, for congregational prayer to be valid for the follower, he must have the specific intention of following that imam.

Specification in Intention for Fard and Wajib Prayers
Ruling on specification in intention for obligatory prayers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the requirement of specification (ta'yin) in intention for fard and wajib prayers and apply it to determine the status of an unspecified prayer.

Core Idea
For fard and wajib prayers, specifying the exact prayer in intention is required; otherwise, it becomes nafl.

This lesson addresses a key aspect of intention in salah: the need to specify which obligatory prayer you are performing. Without specifying, your prayer is still valid but counts as a voluntary (nafl) prayer. This is a distinctive Hanafi position and has practical implications for every prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is being ruled upon? The act is intention (niyyah) in prayer. The ruling: specification (ta'yin) is wajib for fard and wajib prayers.
2
Understand the default
If one merely intends 'prayer', the prayer is considered nafl. Why? Because nafl is the default category when no specification is made.
This is based on the principle that acts of worship are distinguished by intention.
3
Apply the rule
When performing any fard or wajib prayer, you must specifically intend that prayer (e.g., 'I intend to pray the fard of Zuhr'). If you do not, your prayer will be nafl, and you will not fulfill the obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۳۵۴) [۱۲] فرض کا معین کرنا۔ [۱۳] واجب کا معین کرنا، اور نفل کی تعیین شرط نہیں ۔ تشریح : صرف نماز کی نیت کرے تو اس سے نفل نماز ادا ہوگی ، اس لئے فرض ادا کرنا چاہتا ہے تو فرض کی نیت کرنی ہوگی ، اور یہ بھی تعین کرنا ہوگا کہ کون سا فرض ادا کر ہا ہے اسکی بھی تعین کرے، کیوں کہ فرض بہت ہیں، اسی طرح واجب ادا کرنا چاہتا ہوتو اسکی بھی نیت کرنی ہوگی ، ور نہ تو نفل ہو جائیگا۔
Translation: (354) [12] Specifying the fard. [13] Specifying the wajib, and specification is not a condition for nafl. Explanation: If one intends merely prayer, then nafl prayer will be performed. Therefore, if one wants to perform a fard prayer, he must intend fard, and he must also specify which fard he is performing because there are many fard prayers. Similarly, if one wants to perform a wajib prayer, he must intend that specific one; otherwise, it will become nafl.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This lesson is a ruling statement on the requirement of specifying the type of obligatory prayer in the intention. For fard and wajib prayers, one must not only intend the prayer but also determine which specific fard or wajib (e.g., Zuhr, 'Asr, Witr) he is performing. If one merely intends 'prayer', the prayer will be considered nafl (voluntary). This is because the general category 'prayer' defaults to nafl in the absence of specification. The text does not provide explicit proof here; it is based on the principle that intention distinguishes acts of worship.

Key Terms
تعیین (ta'yin): Specification of the particular prayer in intention.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, for any fard or wajib prayer, you must specifically intend that exact prayer in your heart; otherwise, your prayer will be counted as nafl and the obligation will not be fulfilled.

Standing (Qiyam) in Non-Nafl Prayers
Ruling on standing for obligatory and wajib prayers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on qiyam in fard and nafl prayers and identify the dalil from Quran and hadith.

Core Idea
Standing in fard and wajib prayers is obligatory; for nafl, it is not.

This passage clarifies a key distinction in salah: the obligation of standing (qiyam) depends on the type of prayer. While nafl prayers may be performed sitting, fard and wajib prayers require standing. The author provides both Quranic and Prophetic evidence for this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categorisation
The passage distinguishes between nafl and non-nafl prayers. Note that 'non-nafl' includes both fard and wajib prayers.
2
State the ruling for each category
For fard and wajib, qiyam is fard (obligatory). For nafl, it is not fard; sitting is permissible and the prayer is valid.
3
Examine the proofs
The Quranic verse (2:238) commands standing in devotion, and the hadith of Ibn Umar shows the Prophet standing for prayer. Both indicate that standing is an essential part of obligatory prayers.
4
Determine the wajh al-dalalah
The command 'وقوموا' (and stand) is a direct imperative, which in Hanafi usul indicates obligation (wujub) unless there is a qarinah to the contrary. The hadith establishes the practice of the Prophet, confirming the obligation.
The Quranic dalil is qati' al-thubut but zanni al-dalala regarding the exact scope.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider praying zuhr (fard) sitting without excuse: the prayer would be invalid because qiyam is fard. But praying tahajjud sitting is valid because nafl does not require standing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۳۵۵) [۱۴] نفل کے علاوہ سب نمازوں میں قیام کرنا۔ تشریح : نفل نماز میں کھڑا ہونا فرض نہیں ہے، بیٹھ کر بھی نماز پڑھے گا تو نماز ہو جائے گی لیکن فرض نماز میں قیام فرض ہے۔ وجه (۱) کھڑا ہونے کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ وقوموا لله قانتين. (آیت ۲۳۸ سورة البقرة (۲) اس آیت میں ہے کہ چپ چاپ کھڑار ہے ۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں قیام کا ثبوت ہے ، أن ابن عمر قال : كان رسول الله الله ، اذا قام لـلـصـــوـة رفع يديه حتى تكونا بحذو منكبيه ثم كبر ۔ (مسلم شریف، باب استحباب رفع اليدين حذ والمنكبين مع تكبيرة الاحرام ص ۱۶۵ نمبر ۸۶۲/۳۹۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ نماز کے لئے کھڑا ہو۔
Translation: (355) [14] Standing in all prayers except nafl. Explanation: In nafl prayer, standing is not fard; if one prays sitting, the prayer will be valid. But in fard prayer, standing is fard. Proof: (1) The evidence for standing is this verse: 'And stand for Allah in devout obedience.' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:238) This verse commands standing in silence. (2) In this hadith there is evidence for standing: that Ibn Umar said: 'The Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, when he stood for prayer, raised his hands until they were parallel to his shoulders, then said takbir.' (Muslim, chapter on the recommendation of raising hands with takbir al-ihram, p. 165, no. 862/390) From this hadith it is understood that one stands for prayer.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This lesson is a ruling with proof on the requirement of standing (qiyam) in prayers other than nafl. The matn states 'standing in other than nafl'. The commentary clarifies that for nafl, standing is not obligatory; sitting is permissible and prayer is valid. However, for fard prayers, standing is fard (obligatory). There is also a mention of wajib prayers, which are implied by 'other than nafl'. The proof is first a Quranic verse (2:238) which commands standing in submissiveness, and second a hadith showing the Prophet used to stand when starting prayer, indicating that standing is an essential part of non-nafl prayers.

Key Terms
قیام (qiyam): Standing posture in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Standing is obligatory (fard) in fard and wajib prayers, but not in nafl; the Quran and hadith establish this obligation.

Recitation in First Two Rak'ahs of Fard and All Rak'ahs of Nafl/Witr
Ruling on required recitation in different prayers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on required recitation in the first two rak'ahs of fard prayers and in every rak'ah of nafl and witr, and explain the proof from Surah al-Muzzammil 73:20.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, recitation is fard only in the first two rak'ahs of fard, but in every rak'ah of nafl and witr.

This lesson clarifies a fundamental Hanafi ruling: where in the prayer must Quran be recited? While many assume recitation is required in every rak'ah of fard, the Hanafi school limits it to the first two. The passage also explains that nafl and witr prayers require recitation in every rak'ah because they are treated like independent pairs. We will examine the proof from the Quran and a companion hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its general ruling
The act is qira'ah (recitation of Quran) during prayer. The ruling is that it is fard (obligatory) in specific rak'ahs.
2
Distinguish between fard and nafl/witr
For fard prayers, recitation is fard only in the first two rak'ahs. For nafl (supererogatory) and witr (obligatory according to Hanafi), recitation is fard in every rak'ah.
Witr is considered wajib in Hanafi, but treated like nafl for recitation.
3
Understand the basis: shaf' (pair) reasoning
Each two rak'ahs of nafl are considered a separate unit (shaf'), so each rak'ah requires recitation. Witr is treated similarly.
This is why nafl prayers longer than two rak'ahs are not prayed as single units.
4
Examine the primary proof: Quran 73:20
The verse commands 'recite what is easy from it' alongside establishing prayer, indicating obligation.
The word 'faqra'ū' (so recite) is an imperative, implying obligation (wujūb) in Hanafi usul.
5
Note the second proof: hadith on recitation necessity
The hadith (incomplete in our text) states that prayer without recitation is not valid, reinforcing the obligation.
This hadith is general but applied specifically by the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۳۵۶) (۱۵) قرآت کرنا چاہے ایک آیت ہو، فرض کی دونوں رکعتوں میں انفل کی تمام رکعتوں میں، اور وتر میں۔ تشریح : فرض کی پہلی دو رکعتوں میں قرآت کرنا فرض ہے، اس لئے اگر تین رکعت والی نماز ہو ، یا چار رکعت والی نماز ہو تو دوسری دو رکعتوں میں قرآت فرض نہیں ہے نفل کی ہر دو رکعت الگ الگ شفع ہے، اس لئے ہر رکعت میں قرآت فرض ہے، اسی طرح واجب نفل کے درجے میں ہے اسلئے اس کی بھی ہر رکعت میں قرآت فرض ہے۔ تفصیل آگے آئے گی۔ وجه : (۱) فاقرء وا ما تيسر منه واقيموا الصلوة و آتو الزكوة ( آيت ٢٠ سورة المزمل ۷۳ ) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ نماز میں قرآت پڑھنا فرض ہے (۲) اس حدیث میں بھی ہے کہ قرآت کے بغیر نماز نہیں ہوگی ۔ عن ابی سعید قال قال
Translation: (356) (15) Recitation, even if one verse, in the two rak'ahs of fard, in all rak'ahs of nafl, and in witr. Explanation: In the first two rak'ahs of fard, recitation is fard; therefore, if the prayer is three or four rak'ahs, recitation in the remaining rak'ahs is not fard. Each two rak'ahs of nafl are separate pairs (shaf'), so recitation is fard in every rak'ah. Similarly, wajib is in the category of nafl, so recitation is fard in every rak'ah of it. Details will come later. Proof: (1) 'So recite what is easy from it, establish prayer, and give zakah' (Surah al-Muzzammil 73:20) From this verse it is understood that recitation in prayer is fard. (2) In this hadith it is also stated that prayer is not valid without recitation. From Abu Sa'id, he said...
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This lesson is a ruling with proof on the requirement of recitation (qira'ah) in prayer. For fard prayers, recitation (at least one verse) is obligatory only in the first two rak'ahs. In nafl and witr prayers, recitation is fard in every rak'ah. The reasoning is that nafl and witr are treated like pairs (shaf'), where each pair is an independent unit requiring recitation. The proof includes a Quranic verse (73:20) commanding recitation of what is easy, indicating its obligatory nature, and a hadith stating that prayer without recitation is not valid.

Key Terms

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, recitation (qira'ah) is fard in the first two rak'ahs of every fard prayer and in every rak'ah of nafl and witr.

Intention to Follow the Imam and Takbirat al-Ihram
Rulings on takbir al-ihram and intention to follow imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the follower's intention to follow the imam and explain the evidence from the hadith.

Core Idea
The follower must explicitly intend to follow the imam; general prayer intention is insufficient.

This lesson examines two important conditions for the follower (muqtadi) in congregational prayer: the audibility of takbir al-ihram and the specific intention to follow the imam. The Hanafi school derives these rulings from prophetic hadith, emphasizing the necessity of conscious followership. Understanding these conditions ensures the validity of congregational prayer and its reward.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The passage states two rulings: first, the takbir al-ihram must be uttered audibly enough for the person to hear himself; second, the follower must make the intention to follow the imam (niyyat al-mutaba'ah).
The first ruling is qualified as 'according to the most correct view (al-ashahh)'.
2
Locate the hadith proof
The author cites two hadith: the first from Bukhari and Muslim: 'The imam is appointed only to be followed...' and the second from Tirmidhi: 'The imam is a guarantor...'.
The first hadith directly commands following, the second implies a relationship of guarantee.
3
Analyze the legal implication (wajh al-dalalah)
From the command to follow, the Hanafi school infers that the follower must specifically intend to follow, because worship actions require intention. The 'guarantor' hadith reinforces that the follower's prayer is linked to the imam's, necessitating a deliberate connection.
This is the key step: the command to follow (al-i'timam) is interpreted as requiring a specific intention, not just a general prayer intention.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (disagreement)
Some Shafi'i scholars hold that the general intention for the prayer suffices; followership is inherent in the act of praying behind an imam. The Hanafi response is that the hadith's explicit command necessitates a separate intention.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf): according to Hanafis, without specific intention, the prayer is valid as individual but not as congregational.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a follower who intends the fard prayer but does not intend to follow the imam. According to Hanafi, his prayer is valid as an individual prayer, but he does not attain the status of a muqtadi, so he is not covered by the imam's errors.
This highlights the importance of forming the intention correctly when joining the congregation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والنطق بالتحريمة بحيث يسمع نفسه على الاصح (۳۵۳) .ونية المتابعة للمقتدى (۳۵۴) وجه: اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابی ھریرة ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال انما جعل الامام ليؤتم به فلا تختلفوا عليه فاذا كبر فكبر و . (مسلم شریف ، باب ائتمام الماموم بالا مام ، ص ۱۷۶، نمبر ۹۳۰/۴۱۴ / بخاری شریف ، باب انما جعل الامام لیو تم بہ ص ۱۱۳ نمبر ۶۸۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مقتدی کو امام کی مکمل اقتدا کرنی چاہئے ۔ اور اس سے انحراف نہیں کرنا چاہئے ۔ اس لئے امام کی اقتدا کی نیت ضروری ہے (۲) ۔ عن ابي هريرة قال قال رسول الله لا لا لا له الامام ضامن والمؤذن مؤتمن ( ترندی شریف ، باب ما جاء ان الامام ضامن والمؤذن موتمن، ص ۵۸، نمبر ۲۰۷) جب امام ضامن ہوا تو اس کی اقتدا کی نیت بھی کرنی چاہئے۔
And the utterance of the takbir (al-ihram) such that he hears himself, according to the most correct view (353). And the intention of following for the follower (354). Proof: In this hadith... from Abu Hurayra that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'The imam is appointed only to be followed, so do not differ from him. When he says takbir, say takbir.' (Muslim, Bab I'timam al-Ma'mum bi al-Imam, p.176, no.930/414; Bukhari, p.113, no.688) From this hadith it is understood that the follower must completely follow the imam and not deviate from him. Therefore, intention to follow the imam is necessary. (2) From Abu Hurayra: the Messenger of Allah said: 'The imam is a guarantor and the mu'adhdhin is entrusted.' (Tirmidhi, Bab Ma Ja'a an al-Imam Damin, p.58, no.207) Since the imam is a guarantor, intention to follow him must be made.

Commentary
This passage presents two rulings from the chapter on conditions of prayer. First, the takbirat al-ihram must be uttered audibly enough for the person to hear themselves; this is the most correct view. Second, the follower (muqtadi) must make the intention to follow the imam. The author provides proof from two hadiths: the first from Bukhari and Muslim establishes that the imam is to be followed, so the follower must intend to follow. The second from Tirmidhi states that the imam is a guarantor, implying that the follower's prayer is linked to the imam's, necessitating the intention.

Key Terms

تحريمة (tahrimah): The opening takbir (takbirat al-ihram) that begins the prayer.

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the follower's intention to follow the imam?
A) It is sunnah
B) It is wajib
C) It is mustahabb
D) It is not required

Key Takeaway
The follower must explicitly intend to follow the imam, and the takbir al-ihram must be audible to oneself; both are conditions for the validity of congregational prayer in the Hanafi school.

The Fard and Wajib of Quran Recitation in Prayer
Ruling with proof on the obligations of Quran recitation in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the minimum Quran recitation in prayer and distinguish between fard and wajib levels, applying the distinction to a scenario.

Core Idea
Reciting any one verse is fard; Surah Fatiha is wajib – a unique Hanafi hierarchy based on evidence strength.

This lesson explains the Hanafi position on what must be recited in prayer. While many schools insist Surah Fatiha is essential (fard), the Hanafi school distinguishes between a general obligation to recite some Quran (fard) and the specific obligation of Fatiha (wajib). You will see how the Quranic verse and a hadith are interpreted to reach this ruling, and how this differs from the Shafi'i view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is Quran recitation during prayer. The ruling has two components: (1) reciting any one long verse or three short verses is fard (pillar) – without it prayer is invalid. (2) Reciting Surah Fatiha is wajib – omission requires sajdah al-sahw but does not invalidate.
This two-tiered obligation is a distinctive feature of Hanafi fiqh.
2
Locate the dalil
Two proofs: (a) Quran 73:20 'faqra'u ma tayassara minh' – a general command to recite what is easy. (b) Hadith 'La salata liman lam yaqra' bi al-hamd wa surah' – no prayer without Fatiha and a surah.
The Quranic verse is qati al-thubut but zanni al-dalala; the hadith is zanni al-thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Quranic imperative indicates obligation but leaves the amount open; thus any verse suffices for fard. The hadith specifies Fatiha, but as an ahad report, it creates a lesser obligation (wajib) in Hanafi usul.
Hanafi usul distinguishes fard (decisive evidence) from wajib (probable evidence).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school considers the same hadith as proof that Fatiha is fard. They do not accept the fard/wajib distinction and hold that omitting Fatiha invalidates the prayer.
This difference stems from a methodological dispute over the status of ahad hadith.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi. The Quranic verse establishes the fard of general recitation; the hadith, being zanni, makes Fatiha wajib. This is the relied-upon view in the madhhab.
The practical consequence: a prayer without Fatiha is valid but requires sajdah al-sahw if forgotten.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Chapter: Conditions and Pillars of Prayer. And even if only a verse in the two rak'ats of the obligatory prayer and all voluntary and witr prayers (357). And nothing specific from the Quran is designated for the validity of prayer (358). And the follower does not recite, but rather listens and remains silent; if he recites, it is prohibitively disliked. The Messenger of Allah said: 'The key to prayer is purification, its opening is the takbir, and its closing is the taslim; and there is no prayer for one who does not recite al-Hamd (Fatiha) and a surah in an obligatory or any prayer.' (Tirmidhi, chapter on the prohibition and opening of prayer, p. 55, no. 238; Abu Dawud, chapter on the imam after raising his head from the last prostration, p. 98, no. 618). In this hadith, it states that there is no prayer without recitation. Translation (357): For the prayer to be valid, nothing specific from the Quran is designated. Explanation: According to the other imams, reciting Surah Fatiha is obligatory (fard); then only will the prayer be valid, otherwise not. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, reciting Surah Fatiha is obligatory (wajib); if not recited, a deficiency remains for which prostration of forgetfulness becomes necessary, but the prayer will be valid. However, reciting one long verse or three short verses from anywhere is fard; without it, the prayer will not be valid. Proof: (1) The verse: 'So recite what is easy from it [the Quran] and establish prayer and give zakah' (Surah al-Muzzammil, 73:20). This verse indicates to recite from wherever is easy, so reciting any single verse is fard. (2) And reciting Surah Fatiha is wajib; its proof is this hadith: from Abu Sa'id, the Messenger of Allah said: 'The key to prayer is purification, its opening is the takbir, and its closing is the taslim; and there is no prayer for one who does not recite al-Hamd (Fatiha) and a surah in an obligatory or any prayer.' In this hadith, it states that prayer is not valid without reciting Fatiha, so reciting Fatiha is made wajib.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school regarding the obligation of Quran recitation in prayer. The author begins by stating the ruling: even if only one verse is recited in the obligatory two rak'ats, and in all voluntary and witr prayers, no specific Quranic portion is designated for validity. The follower does not recite but listens and remains silent; reciting behind the imam is prohibitively disliked. The author then presents a hadith establishing the importance of recitation. The commentary explains the Hanafi position clearly: unlike other imams who consider Surah Fatiha fard, Imam Abu Hanifa holds that Fatiha is wajib, and its omission requires sajdah al-sahw but does not invalidate the prayer. The fard (obligatory) element for recitation is any one long verse or three short verses from anywhere in the Quran, based on the verse 'Fa'qra'u ma tayassara minh' (So recite what is easy). The hadith 'La salata liman lam yaqra' bi al-hamd wa surah' is interpreted by the Hanafis as indicating wujub (obligatory) for Fatiha, not fard, because it is a hadith ahad, which in Hanafi usul imposes a lesser degree of obligation (wajib) compared to mutawatir texts (which impose fard). Thus, the Hanafi school distinguishes between the fard of reciting some Quran and the wajib of reciting Fatiha specifically.

Key Terms
فرض (fard): An obligation established by a decisive (qati) text; its omission invalidates the act without compensation.
واجب (wajib): An obligation established by a zanni text (like ahad hadith); its omission requires compensation (e.g., sajdah al-sahw) but does not invalidate the act.
آية (ayah): A verse of the Quran; here, a long verse or three short verses constitute the minimum fard recitation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid but sajdah al-sahw is required if forgotten.
C) The prayer is invalid only if omitted intentionally.
D) The prayer is valid and no action is needed.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uniquely distinguishes fard (any verse) from wajib (Fatiha) in prayer recitation, based on differing strengths of evidence.

Follower Should Remain Silent During Imam's Recitation
Ruling with dalil on follower's silence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a follower reciting behind the imam and identify the Quranic and hadith proofs that support the Hanafi position.

Core Idea
The follower must remain silent; the imam’s recitation suffices — recitation behind the imam is makruh tahrimi.

In congregational prayer, the role of the follower is to listen and be silent. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that the follower should not recite the Quran behind the imam, whether the prayer is loud or silent. We will explore the textual proofs from the Quran and multiple hadiths, as well as the respectful difference of the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what action is being ruled upon (the follower's recitation) and its hukm level (makruh tahrimi).
Also note the linked obligation: silence and listening are wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the primary evidence: Quran 7:204 and hadiths from the text that command silence and indicate the imam's recitation suffices.
The Quranic proof is qat'i al-thubut; hadiths are ahad but strong.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the dalil proves the ruling. For example, the imperative 'listen and be silent' directly prohibits recitation.
The hadith 'Whoever has an imam, the imam's recitation is recitation for him' shows sufficiency.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the Shafi'i school's position that requires the follower to recite Fatiha in silent prayers.
The ikhtilaf arises from interpreting general evidence vs. specific exemptions.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Understand why the Hanafi school prefers silence: specific hadiths qualify the general command, and the imam's recitation fulfills the obligation.
The mufta bihi is silence in both loud and silent prayers.

(مسلم شریف، باب تھی الماموم عن جهره بالقراءة خلف الامام ، ص ۱۶۹، نمبر ۳۹۸/ ۸۸۸/ابو داؤد شریف، باب من رأى القراءة اذا لم تجبر ، ص ۱۲۸ نمبر (۸۲۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سری نماز میں بھی قرآت نہ کرے۔ (۶) عن ابي هريرة ..... مالي انازع القرآن قال فانتهى الناس عن القراءة مع رسول الله لل الله فيما جهر فيه - ( ابوداؤد شریف، باب من رأى القراءة اذالم يسجير ، ص ۱۲۷، نمبر ۸۲۶ ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی ترک القراءة خلف الامام اذا جهر الامام بالقرائہ ہی اے، نمبر ۳۱۲ ) ان احادیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ جہری نماز میں قرآت سے رک گئے ، تاہم اتنا معلوم ہوا کہ قرآت خلف الامام مناسب نہیں ہے۔ امام محمد کی ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ سری نماز میں قرآت خلف الامام کرلے ، احتیاط کے لئے یہ اچھا سمجھا گیا ہے۔ ہدایہ کی عبارت یہ ہے۔ویستحسن على سبيل الاحتياط فيما يروى عن محمد هدايه ج اول ، فصل فی القرآة ص ۱۲۱ نمبر ۳۳۰)
Translation (358): The follower should not recite, but rather listen and remain silent; and if he recites, it is prohibitively disliked. Explanation: In congregation, the recitation of the imam is sufficient for the follower; therefore the follower should not recite Quran behind him, but listen and remain silent; if he recites, it is prohibitively disliked. Proof: (1) The verse: 'And when the Quran is recited, listen to it and remain silent, that you may receive mercy' (Surah al-A'raf 7:204). This verse commands listening and being silent. (2) From Abu Hurairah: The Messenger of Allah said: 'The imam is appointed to be followed; when he says takbir, say takbir; when he recites, be silent.' (Ibn Majah, chapter: when the imam recites, be silent, p. 120, no. 1846; Nasa'i, chapter: interpretation of the verse 'and when the Quran is recited...', p. 128, no. 922; Muslim, chapter: tashahhud in prayer, p. 172, no. 905/404). This hadith shows that during recitation the follower should be silent. (3) From Jabir: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever has an imam, the recitation of the imam is recitation for him.' (Ibn Majah, p. 120, no. 850; Dar Qutni, chapter: mention of his saying 'whoever has an imam', p. 1321, no. 1220). (4) From Abu Darda' who heard: The Messenger of Allah was asked: 'Is there recitation in every prayer?' He said: 'Yes.' A man from the Ansar said: 'Is this obligatory?' Then he turned to me and I was the closest of the people to him, and said: 'I think that the imam, when he leads the people, suffices them.' (Nasa'i, chapter: sufficiency of the follower with the imam's recitation, p. 128, no. 924; Dar Qutni, vol. 1, p. 326, no. 1248). This also shows that the imam's recitation is sufficient for the followers; it shows that when the imam recites Fatiha, it is as if the follower recites it; he does not remain without Fatiha. (5) And if the follower recites, it is disliked; its proof is this hadith: From 'Imran ibn Husain: The Messenger of Allah prayed Dhuhr, and a man started reciting behind him: 'Sabbih isma rabbika al-a'la.' When he finished, he said: 'Which of you recited?' or 'Who is the reciter?' The man said: 'I did.' He said: 'I thought that some of you were contending with me (in recitation).' (Muslim, chapter: prohibition of the follower reciting aloud behind the imam, p. 169, no. 398/888; Abu Dawud, chapter: on recitation when not loud, p. 128, no. 828). This hadith shows that even in silent prayers, the follower should not recite. (6) From Abu Hurairah: '...Why do I contend with the Quran?' So the people stopped reciting with the Messenger of Allah when he recited aloud. (Abu Dawud, chapter: on recitation when not loud, p. 127, no. 826; Tirmidhi, chapter: on abandoning recitation behind the imam when the imam recites aloud, no. 312). These hadiths show that in loud prayers, they stopped recitation. At the very least, it is understood that recitation behind the imam is not appropriate. There is a narration from Imam Muhammad that in silent prayers, the follower may recite; this is considered commendable as a precaution. The text of Hidayah states: 'It is considered commendable as a precaution according to what is narrated from Muhammad.' (Hidayah, vol. 1, chapter on recitation, p. 121, no. 330).
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the follower (muqtadi) in congregational prayer. The primary ruling is that the follower must not recite the Quran behind the imam; instead, he should listen attentively and remain silent. If he recites, it is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). The author provides multiple proofs: firstly, the Quranic command in Surah al-A'raf (7:204) to listen and be silent when the Quran is recited. Second, several hadiths explicitly command silence during the imam's recitation and indicate that the imam's recitation suffices for the follower. The hadith from Abu Hurairah states that the imam is appointed to be followed; when he recites, be silent. The hadith from Jabir and Abu Darda' emphasizes that the imam's recitation is sufficient for the followers. Another hadith from 'Imran ibn Husain shows that even in silent (sirr) prayers, the follower should not recite aloud. The author then notes a narration from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani that in silent prayers, the follower may recite (presumably quietly), and this is considered commendable as a precaution, as mentioned in Al-Hidayah. The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school, however, is that the follower should not recite at all behind the imam, whether in loud or silent prayers. The follower's obligation of recitation is fulfilled by the imam's recitation. The hadiths are interpreted to mean that the follower is absolved of recitation due to the imam's burden. The Hanafi school thus differs from other schools (like Shafi'i) that require the follower to recite Fatiha in silent prayers.

Key Terms
مؤتم (mu'tamm (muqtadi)): The follower in congregational prayer who prays behind an imam.
مکروہ تحریمی (makruh tahrimi): An act that is prohibitively disliked, closer to haram, based on a zanni evidence. It is sinful to commit it but does not invalidate the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a follower recites Quran behind the imam in a loud (jahr) prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) It is mustahab (recommended)
B) It is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked)
C) It is wajib (obligatory)
D) It is mubah (permissible)

Key Takeaway
The follower must remain silent during the imam's recitation; the imam's recitation suffices, and any recitation by the follower is makruh tahrimi.

The Obligation of Ruku' in Prayer
Ruling that ruku' is a fard (obligatory) component of prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of ruku' in prayer and identify the Quranic evidence that establishes its obligation.

Core Idea
Ruku' is fard in prayer, proven by explicit Quranic command.

In this lesson, we examine a brief but foundational ruling from Thamaratun Najah: ruku' (bowing) is an obligatory component of prayer. The author provides two Quranic verses as evidence, demonstrating that the obligation is rooted in divine command. Understanding this ruling is essential because missing ruku' invalidates the prayer entirely.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act the passage is ruling upon and what the ruling is. The passage states that ruku' is fard (obligatory).
The ruling is clear: ruku' is not optional; it is a legal requirement.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence cited. The author quotes two Quranic verses: Surah al-Hajj 22:77 and Surah al-Baqarah 2:43.
Both verses contain the imperative form 'ark'u' (bow).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the evidence proves the ruling. The imperative 'ark'u' is a command, and in Hanafi usul, commands indicate obligation (fard).
The context of prayer confirms that the command is for prayer.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Check if there is disagreement. The passage indicates no ikhtilaf; ruku' is unanimously considered fard across madhhabs.
This ruling is muttafaq alayh (agreed upon).
5
Evaluate the Hanafi position
Confirm the operative ruling. In the Hanafi school, ruku' is a rukn (pillar) of prayer; its omission invalidates the rak'ah and the prayer.
There is no compensation for missing a rukn; the prayer must be repeated.

Source Text

ترجمه : (۳۵۹) [۱۶] اور رکوع کرنا۔ تشریح : نماز میں رکوع کرنا فرض ہے۔ وجه : (۱) رکوع اور سجدہ دونوں کے فرض ہونے کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ یا ایها الذين آمنوا اركعوا واسجدوا واعبدواربكم. ( آیت ۷۷،سورۃ الج ۲۲)(۲) اور واقيموا الصلوۃ و آتو الزكوة واركعوا مع الراكعين (آیت۴۳ سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ رکوع اور سجدہ فرض ہیں۔
Translation (359): [16] And to perform ruku' (bowing). Explanation: Performing ruku' in prayer is fard. Proof: (1) The evidence for both ruku' and sujud being fard is this verse: 'O you who have believed, bow and prostrate and worship your Lord' (Surah al-Hajj 22:77). (2) And 'Establish prayer and give zakah and bow with those who bow' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:43). From these verses it is understood that ruku' and sujud are fard.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage is a brief ruling statement with proof that ruku' (bowing) is an obligatory (fard) component of prayer. The author simply asserts that ruku' is fard and provides two Quranic verses as evidence. The first verse from Surah al-Hajj contains the imperative 'ark'u' (bow) and 'usjudu' (prostrate), which are commands indicating obligation (fard). The second verse from Surah al-Baqarah commands the believers to bow with those who bow, reinforcing the obligation. There is no mention of any detailed conditions for ruku' such as the minimum bow or dhikr; later texts discuss those. This passage assumes the reader knows that ruku' is performed in each rak'ah after recitation. In the Hanafi school, ruku' is one of the pillars (arkan) of prayer; its omission intentionally or forgetfully invalidates that rak'ah and requires repeating it or performing sajdah al-sahw.

Key Terms
رکوع (ruku'): Bowing in prayer, lowering the body so that hands reach the knees, with back straight; a pillar (rukn) of prayer.

Key Takeaway
Ruku' is a fard pillar of prayer established by explicit Quranic command; its omission invalidates the prayer.

Salah — Prayer

Ruku' is Fard in Prayer
Ruling with Qur'anic proof on ruku'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that ruku' is fard (obligatory) and cite the Qur'anic evidence from Surah al-Hajj 22:77 and Surah al-Baqarah 2:43.

Core Idea
Ruku' is fard by direct Qur'anic command; omission invalidates the prayer.

This passage opens with a clear ruling: ruku' (bowing) in prayer is fard. The author provides two Qur'anic verses as the basis. Understanding that ruku' is a pillar (rukn) is essential for every Hanafi—missing it intentionally or unintentionally breaks the prayer and requires complete repetition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text states 'رکوع کرنا فرض ہے' (ruku' is fard). Confirm the act is ruku' and the hukm is fard.
Fard means obligatory; omission invalidates the act.
2
Locate the Qur'anic proof
The author cites two verses: (1) 'اركعوا واسجدوا' from Surah al-Hajj 22:77, (2) 'واركعوا مع الراكعين' from Surah al-Baqarah 2:43. These contain the imperative 'irka'u' (bow).
Imperative form indicates obligation in Hanafi usul.
3
Understand the usul principle
In Hanafi usul, al-amr yufidu al-wujub – the command form (f'il amr) signifies obligation unless there is a qarinah (contextual indicator) to the contrary. No such indicator exists here.
This principle applies to both verses; hence ruku' is fard.

Translation: (359) [16] And performing ruku'. Explanation: Ruku' in prayer is fard. Evidence: (1) The evidence for both ruku' and sujud being fard is this verse: 'O you who believe, bow and prostrate and worship your Lord' (Surah al-Hajj 22:77). (2) And 'Establish prayer and give zakat and bow with those who bow' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:43). From this verse it is understood that ruku' and sujud are fard. Translation: (360) [17] Performing sujud on something that has mass (hajm) and on which the forehead rests, even if it is on one's hand or the edge of one's garment, provided the place of placement is pure. Explanation: Here he says three things: [1] One thing is to perform sujud. [2] The second thing is that sujud in the air is not sufficient, nor is placing the forehead on something soft that gets compressed; rather, one must place the forehead on something that has some mass and on which the forehead rests firmly, like the ground or a board etc. [3] And the third thing he says is that if one performs sujud on a bag or the edge of a garment, the sujud is still valid. Evidence: (1) In this hadith from Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi: 'The Prophet (ﷺ) used to, when he prostrated, firmly place his nose and forehead on the ground, keep his arms away from his sides, and place his palms level with his shoulders.' (Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi al-sujud 'ala al-jabha wa al-anf, p. 74, no. 270; Abu Dawud, Bab al-rajul yasjudu 'ala thawbi-hi, p. 105, no. 660). This hadith mentions that he used to firmly place his nose and forehead on the ground. (2) In this saying of a Companion: 'Umar said: 'When a man places his forehead on the ground, it suffices him.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, Fi adna ma yujzi min al-ruku' wa al-sujud, vol. 1, p. 226, no. 2584, no. 2580). This effect shows that placing the forehead on the ground suffices for sujud. (3) Sujud on the edge of a garment is permissible with this hadith: Anas ibn Malik said: 'We used to pray with the Prophet (ﷺ) and one of us would place the edge of his garment on the place of sujud due to intense heat.' (Bukhari, Bab al-sujud 'ala al-thawb fi shidda al-harr, p. 68, no. 1385; Abu Dawud, Bab al-rajul yasjudu 'ala thawbi-hi, p. 105, no. 660). This hadith shows that sujud on the edge of a turban suffices. (4) He heard Abu Hurayra say: 'The Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) used to prostrate on the bulk of his turban.' (Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-sujud 'ala al-'imama, vol. 1, p. 303, no. 1566). This hadith mentions that he prostrated on the turban. Lexicon: 'hajm' refers to the solidity of something. 'Tastaqirru' means it settles. Translation: (361) And in sujud, it is wajib to place both the nose and forehead, and confining to only the nose is not valid. However, if there is an excuse on the forehead, then it is valid. Explanation: In sujud, placing both the nose and forehead on the ground is wajib; one alone will not suffice, or confining to only the nose is not valid. However, if there is an excuse on the forehead, then placing only the nose suffices for sujud. Evidence: (1) From Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi: 'The Prophet (ﷺ) used to, when he prostrated, firmly place his nose and forehead on the ground, and keep his arms away from his sides, and place his palms level with his shoulders.' (Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi al-sujud 'ala al-jabha wa al-anf, p. 74, no. 270). This hadith mentions that he prostrated on the nose and forehead. (2) From Ibn 'Abbas who said: 'The Prophet (ﷺ) said: I have been commanded to prostrate on seven bones: on the forehead – and he pointed to his nose – and the hands, the knees, and the edges of the feet.' (Bukhari, Bab al-sujud 'ala ... )
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage is from Thamaratun Najah, a Hanafi fiqh work, covering rulings on ruku' and sujud. The author first states (359) that ruku' is fard, providing Qur'anic evidence from Surah al-Hajj 22:77 and Surah al-Baqarah 2:43, which command bowing and prostrating. Then (360) details the conditions for sujud: it must be on something with substance (hajm) that allows the forehead to rest firmly. Sujud in the air or on something soft that compresses completely is invalid. However, sujud on one's hand or the edge of one's garment is valid if the place is pure. The author cites hadith from Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi showing the Prophet placed his nose and forehead on the ground, and from Anas ibn Malik and Abu Hurayra about prostrating on garment edges and turbans. Finally (361), it is wajib to place both the nose and forehead in sujud. If only the nose is used without excuse, sujud is invalid; but if the forehead has an excuse (e.g., a wound), then only the nose suffices. Evidence includes the hadith of seven bones from Ibn 'Abbas where the forehead is mentioned and the Prophet pointed to his nose, indicating both are required. The Hanafi position is clear: sujud requires both, but the forehead is the primary organ; the nose is a support. This differs from some schools that consider the nose recommended but not obligatory.

Key Terms
رکوع (ruku'): Bowing in prayer: bending the back and placing hands on knees.
فرض (fard): Obligatory; an act that is conclusively proven by qat'i evidence, omission invalidates the act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the evidence that ruku' is fard according to the Hanafi school?
A) Hadith from Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi
B) Qur'anic verses from Surah al-Hajj and al-Baqarah
C) Consensus of the Companions
D) Analogy to sujud

Key Takeaway
Ruku' is a fard pillar of prayer, proven by the Qur'anic imperative, and its omission invalidates the prayer.

Conditions for Sujud: The Requirement of Mass (Hajm)
Condition for sujud: requirement of mass and permissibility of garment edge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition that sujud must be performed on a surface with mass (hajm) that allows the forehead to rest, and identify exceptions like the edge of a garment.

Core Idea
Sujud requires a firm, non-compressible surface; soft or floating surfaces do not suffice.

The second section of the passage (number 360) details the physical requirement for sujud: the forehead must rest on something with substance (hajm), not on air or something that compresses completely. The author also clarifies that sujud on the hand or the edge of a garment is valid if the place is pure, based on prophetic practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for sujud
The text states that sujud must be on something that has 'hajm' (mass) and on which the forehead rests (تستقر). This excludes air and very soft surfaces.
Hajm refers to solidity; e.g., earth, wood, or compacted surfaces.
2
Recognize the exceptions
Sujud on one's own hand or the edge of one's garment is permitted, provided the place of placement is ritually pure (tahir).
This is based on hadith where the Prophet (ﷺ) prostrated on the edge of his turban.
3
Understand the evidence
The author cites hadith of Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi showing the Prophet firmly placed his nose and forehead on the ground, and hadith of Anas ibn Malik and Abu Hurayra about prostrating on garments due to heat.
These show that a barrier between forehead and ground does not invalidate if it is not excessively thick.

تشریح : سجدہ میں ناک اور پیشانی دونوں کو زمین پر لگانا واجب ہے، صرف ایک سے کام نہیں چلے گا، یا صرف ناک پر اکتفاء کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے، البتہ اگر پیشانی پر کوئی عذر ہو تو صرف ناک رکھ دینے سے سجدہ ادا ہو جائے گا۔
وجه : (ا) عن ابي حميد الساعدي : أن النبي الا الله كان اذا سجد أمكن أنفه و جبهته من الارض و نحى يديه عن جنبيه ، ووضع كفيه حذو منكبيه . ( ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء في السجود علی الجبھۃ والانف، ص۷۴، نمبر ۲۷۰) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ناک اور پیشانی پر سجدہ کرے۔ (۲) عن ابن عباس قال قال النبي لا امرت ان اسجد على سبعة اعـظـم عـلـى الجبهة - واشار بيده على انفه - واليدين والركبتين واطراف القدمین (بخاری شریف، باب السجود علی
Translation: (359) [16] And performing ruku'. Explanation: Ruku' in prayer is fard. Evidence: (1) The evidence for both ruku' and sujud being fard is this verse: 'O you who believe, bow and prostrate and worship your Lord' (Surah al-Hajj 22:77). (2) And 'Establish prayer and give zakat and bow with those who bow' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:43). From this verse it is understood that ruku' and sujud are fard. Translation: (360) [17] Performing sujud on something that has mass (hajm) and on which the forehead rests, even if it is on one's hand or the edge of one's garment, provided the place of placement is pure. Explanation: Here he says three things: [1] One thing is to perform sujud. [2] The second thing is that sujud in the air is not sufficient, nor is placing the forehead on something soft that gets compressed; rather, one must place the forehead on something that has some mass and on which the forehead rests firmly, like the ground or a board etc. [3] And the third thing he says is that if one performs sujud on a bag or the edge of a garment, the sujud is still valid. Evidence: (1) In this hadith from Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi: 'The Prophet (ﷺ) used to, when he prostrated, firmly place his nose and forehead on the ground, keep his arms away from his sides, and place his palms level with his shoulders.' (Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi al-sujud 'ala al-jabha wa al-anf, p. 74, no. 270; Abu Dawud, Bab al-rajul yasjudu 'ala thawbi-hi, p. 105, no. 660). This hadith mentions that he used to firmly place his nose and forehead on the ground. (2) In this saying of a Companion: 'Umar said: 'When a man places his forehead on the ground, it suffices him.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, Fi adna ma yujzi min al-ruku' wa al-sujud, vol. 1, p. 226, no. 2584, no. 2580). This effect shows that placing the forehead on the ground suffices for sujud. (3) Sujud on the edge of a garment is permissible with this hadith: Anas ibn Malik said: 'We used to pray with the Prophet (ﷺ) and one of us would place the edge of his garment on the place of sujud due to intense heat.' (Bukhari, Bab al-sujud 'ala al-thawb fi shidda al-harr, p. 68, no. 1385; Abu Dawud, Bab al-rajul yasjudu 'ala thawbi-hi, p. 105, no. 660). This hadith shows that sujud on the edge of a turban suffices. (4) He heard Abu Hurayra say: 'The Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) used to prostrate on the bulk of his turban.' (Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-sujud 'ala al-'imama, vol. 1, p. 303, no. 1566). This hadith mentions that he prostrated on the turban. Lexicon: 'hajm' refers to the solidity of something. 'Tastaqirru' means it settles. Translation: (361) And in sujud, it is wajib to place both the nose and forehead, and confining to only the nose is not valid. However, if there is an excuse on the forehead, then it is valid. Explanation: In sujud, placing both the nose and forehead on the ground is wajib; one alone will not suffice, or confining to only the nose is not valid. However, if there is an excuse on the forehead, then placing only the nose suffices for sujud. Evidence: (1) From Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi: 'The Prophet (ﷺ) used to, when he prostrated, firmly place his nose and forehead on the ground, and keep his arms away from his sides, and place his palms level with his shoulders.' (Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi al-sujud 'ala al-jabha wa al-anf, p. 74, no. 270). This hadith mentions that he prostrated on the nose and forehead. (2) From Ibn 'Abbas who said: 'The Prophet (ﷺ) said: I have been commanded to prostrate on seven bones: on the forehead – and he pointed to his nose – and the hands, the knees, and the edges of the feet.' (Bukhari, Bab al-sujud 'ala ... )
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage is from Thamaratun Najah, a Hanafi fiqh work, covering rulings on ruku' and sujud. The author first states (359) that ruku' is fard, providing Qur'anic evidence from Surah al-Hajj 22:77 and Surah al-Baqarah 2:43, which command bowing and prostrating. Then (360) details the conditions for sujud: it must be on something with substance (hajm) that allows the forehead to rest firmly. Sujud in the air or on something soft that compresses completely is invalid. However, sujud on one's hand or the edge of one's garment is valid if the place is pure. The author cites hadith from Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi showing the Prophet placed his nose and forehead on the ground, and from Anas ibn Malik and Abu Hurayra about prostrating on garment edges and turbans. Finally (361), it is wajib to place both the nose and forehead in sujud. If only the nose is used without excuse, sujud is invalid; but if the forehead has an excuse (e.g., a wound), then only the nose suffices. Evidence includes the hadith of seven bones from Ibn 'Abbas where the forehead is mentioned and the Prophet pointed to his nose, indicating both are required. The Hanafi position is clear: sujud requires both, but the forehead is the primary organ; the nose is a support. This differs from some schools that consider the nose recommended but not obligatory.

Key Terms
حجم (hajm): Mass or solidity; something that does not compress completely under pressure, allowing the forehead to rest.
تستقر (tastaqirru): It settles; the forehead must come to rest on the surface.
سجدہ (sujud): Prostration in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Is sujud valid on a pile of soft cotton that sinks completely under the forehead?
A) Yes, because the forehead makes contact.
B) No, because the cotton lacks hajm; the forehead does not rest.
C) Yes, because the cotton is pure.
D) No, only if the cotton is najis.

Key Takeaway
Sujud must be performed on a surface with mass that allows the forehead to settle; sujud on a thin barrier is permissible.

Sujud Requires Both Nose and Forehead (Wajib)
Ruling with hadith proof on wajib of nose and forehead

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that placing both nose and forehead in sujud is wajib, state the evidence from the hadith of seven bones, and identify the exception when the forehead has an excuse.

Core Idea
Both nose and forehead are required in sujud; the nose is not optional—omission without excuse invalidates the sujud.

In the third segment (number 361), the author addresses a common nuance: must the nose also touch the ground in sujud? The Hanafi ruling is that placing both nose and forehead is wajib (necessary). The evidence comes from the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas where the Prophet commanded prostration on seven bones, pointing to his nose after mentioning the forehead. The text also provides an exception: if the forehead has a genuine excuse (e.g., wound), sujud on the nose alone suffices.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The text says: 'سجدہ میں ناک اور پیشانی دونوں ٹکانا واجب ہے' (placing both nose and forehead in sujud is wajib).
Wajib means obligatory but not at the level of fard; omission requires compensation.
2
Identify the evidence
The author cites the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas: 'I have been commanded to prostrate on seven bones: on the forehead – and he pointed to his nose – and the hands...'
The Prophet's pointing links the nose to the command for the forehead.
3
Understand the exception
If the forehead has an excuse (e.g., a wound), then sujud on the nose alone is valid.
This shows that the forehead is the primary organ; the nose is a support.
4
Contrast with other schools
Shafi'i and Maliki consider the nose sunnah; Hanbali consider both fard. Hanafi takes a middle position: wajib.
The difference in ruling reflects different usul principles on how to understand the hadith.

Commentary
This passage is from Thamaratun Najah, a Hanafi fiqh work, covering rulings on ruku' and sujud. The author cites hadith from Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi showing the Prophet placed his nose and forehead on the ground, and from Anas ibn Malik and Abu Hurayra about prostrating on garment edges and turbans. Key Terms
واجب (wajib): Obligatory but based on zanni evidence; omission requires compensation (sajdah al-sahw) if unintentional, and invalidates if intentional.
عذر (udhr): Excuse that permits relaxation of a requirement; here, a legitimate reason (e.g., wound, bandage) that allows sujud on nose alone.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, a person prostrates with only the nose touching the ground (forehead raised), and he has no excuse. What is the ruling on his sujud?
A) Valid because the nose contacts the ground.

Key Takeaway
Sujud requires both nose and forehead; the nose is a wajib component, not optional, except when the forehead has a valid excuse.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
