Exposure of a Quarter of a Limb Invalidates Prayer
Ruling on exposure of quarter of a limb

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the minimum exposure of the 'awrah that invalidates prayer and explain the proof from the hadith of wiping the forelock.

Core Idea
Exposing a quarter of an 'awrah limb invalidates prayer, as a quarter is legally significant (kathir).

One of the key conditions for the validity of prayer is covering the 'awrah. But what if a small part becomes exposed accidentally? The Hanafi school has a precise threshold: a quarter of a limb. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the proof from the Prophet's (ﷺ) practice, and the difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions on this issue.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is exposure of the 'awrah during prayer. The ruling: if a quarter of a limb is exposed, the prayer becomes invalid. Note that the condition is covering the 'awrah, and its violation nullifies the prayer.
The ruling applies whether the exposure is intentional or unintentional, as long as it lasts for the duration of one rukn (e.g., one recitation of 'Subhanallah').
2
Locate the primary dalil
The author cites two hadiths. The first is from 'Urwah ibn al-Mughira, where the Prophet (ﷺ) wiped his forelock (approximately a quarter of his head) and considered it sufficient for wiping the head in wudu. The second is from 'Amir ibn Sa'd, where the Prophet called one-third 'kathir'.
These are ahad hadith, so their thubut (transmission) is zanni, but they are accepted as evidence.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof applies)
The first hadith is used via isharat al-nass (indication of the text): since wiping a quarter of the head suffices for the whole head, a quarter of a limb is considered a significant amount (kathir). Thus, exposing a quarter of an 'awrah limb is like exposing the whole limb. The second hadith reinforces that one-third is kathir, implying that a quarter is also kathir.
Imam Abu Hanifa used the one-third threshold from the second hadith, but the relied-upon position adopts the quarter from the first.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Hanifa considered one-third as the minimum 'kathir' for exposure, based on the hadith where the Prophet called one-third 'kathir'. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) considered one-quarter, based on the wiping hadith. The text follows the Sahibayn's view.
The practical difference: a piece of clothing exposing exactly one-third of a limb would invalidate prayer according to Abu Hanifa, but not according to the Sahibayn (since it is less than a quarter? Actually one-third is greater than a quarter, so it would also invalidate. Wait: if one-third is exposed, it is more than a quarter, so both agree it invalidates. The difference occurs for exposures between one-quarter and one-third? Let's clarify: For Abu Hanifa, kathir is one-third or more. So exposure of one-quarter to less than one-third is not kathir for him. For the Sahibayn, kathir is one-quarter or more. So for exposure of one-quarter, the Sahibayn say invalid, Abu Hanifa says valid. The text adopts the Sahibayn's stricter view.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position for fatwa is that exposure of a quarter of a limb invalidates prayer. This is the view of the Sahibayn and is adopted by later Hanafi scholars.
This is the operative ruling in Hanafi fiqh today.

Source Text

(۳۸۲) وكشف ربع عضو من اعضاء العورة يمنع صحة الصلوة 
ترجمه : (۳۲) ستر عورت کے اعضاء میں سے چوتھائی عضو کے کھلنے سے نماز صحیح نہیں ہوگی۔
تشریح : نماز میں ستر عورت کھل جائے تو نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی اسی اصول کے تحت فرماتے ہیں کہ ایک عضو کی چوتھائی بھی کھل جائے تو پورے ایک عضو کے کھلنے کے قائم مقام ہو جائے گا اور نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی۔
وجه : (۱) چوتھائی عضو کثیر ہے۔ اور اس حدیث کے اشارۃ النص سے استدلال فرمایا کہ چوتھائی سرسح کرنے کو پورا سر کافی سمجھا گیا
۔ حدیث یہ ہے ۔ عن عروة بن المغيرة بن شعبة ، عن ابيه قال : تخلف رسول الله علم و تخلفت معه، فلما قضى حاجته ..... ومسح بناصيته ، و على العمامة ، و على خفيه ، (مسلم شریف، باب المسح على الناصية ، والعمامة ص ۱۳۴، نمبر ۶۳۳/۲۷۴ ، ابو داود شریف باب المسح علی الخفین ہیں ۲۲، نمبر ۱۵۰) اس حدیث میں پورے سر کے بجائے پیشانی کی ص مقدار، یعنی چوتھائی سرمسح کر لینا کافی قرار دیا۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عامر بن سعد عن ابيه قال : مرض مرضا .... قال : الثلث ، قال : ((الثلث، الثلث كثير ) ) ( ابوداود شریف، باب ما جاء فيما يجوز للموصی فی ماله ، ص ۴۱۶، نمبر ۲۸۶۴) اس حدیث میں تہائی کو کثیر کہا ہے اسلئے تہائی عضو کے کھلنے سے امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک نماز نہیں ہوگی۔
(382) And the exposure of a quarter of a limb from the limbs of the 'awrah prevents the validity of prayer. Translation: The opening of a quarter of a limb from the parts of the 'awrah will make the prayer invalid. Commentary: If the 'awrah is uncovered in prayer, the prayer becomes invalid. Accordingly, it is stated that if a quarter of a limb is exposed, it is considered as the whole limb being exposed, and the prayer becomes invalid. Proof: (1) A quarter of a limb is considered significant (kathir). The author deduces from the indication of the text (isharat al-nass) of the hadith that wiping a quarter of the head is sufficient for the whole head. The hadith: 'Urwah ibn al-Mughirah from his father: The Prophet (peace be upon him) fell behind ... and he wiped over his forelock (nasiah) and over his turban and over his khuffs.' (Muslim, Abu Dawud). In this hadith, wiping only the forelock (approximately a quarter of the head) is considered sufficient for the entire head. (2) Another hadith: 'Amir ibn Sa'd from his father: He was ill ... He said: One-third, he said: One-third, and one-third is large (kathir).' (Abu Dawud). In this hadith, one-third is called 'kathir', therefore according to Imam Abu Hanifa, exposure of one-third of a limb would also invalidate prayer (since one-third is greater than a quarter).
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the effect of exposing a part of the 'awrah in prayer. It states that if any 'awrah limb is exposed to the extent of a quarter of that limb, the prayer is invalid. The commentary explains that this is based on the principle that a quarter of a limb is considered significant (kathir), thus it stands in place of the whole limb. The author provides two proofs: first, the hadith where the Prophet wiped only his forelock (a quarter of the head) and it was accepted as valid for the entire head. This is used as an indication (isharat al-nass) that a quarter is considered a significant amount. Second, a hadith where the Prophet called one-third 'kathir', implying that anything a quarter or more is also 'kathir'. The author notes that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, exposure of one-third would also invalidate prayer, but the relied-upon position is that a quarter is the threshold. In Hanafi fiqh, this ruling applies to all 'awrah limbs in prayer; if less than a quarter is exposed, the prayer remains valid (unless it is done intentionally).

Key Terms
ربع عضو (rub' 'udw): One quarter of a limb from the 'awrah.
کثیر (kathir): A significant amount, legally defined as a quarter or more for exposure rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Any part of a limb
B) One quarter of a limb
C) One half of a limb
D) One third of a limb

Key Takeaway
Exposure of a quarter or more of an 'awrah limb invalidates prayer; the relied-upon Hanafi position is the quarter threshold derived from the hadith of wiping the forelock.

Scattered Exposure of 'Awrah: Cumulative Quarter Rule
Ruling on exposure from multiple spots adding up to quarter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on scattered 'awrah exposure to determine the validity of salah when multiple spots total a quarter of the smallest exposed limb.

Core Idea
Scattered 'awrah exposure cumulatively counts: if total equals a quarter of the smallest exposed limb, salah is invalid.

In Hanafi fiqh, covering the 'awrah is a condition for valid salah. While a single spot of exposure equal to a quarter of a limb invalidates, what if the exposure occurs in multiple separate spots? This lesson extends the quarter principle to scattered exposure, a matter of juristic reasoning (qiyas) directly derived from the established ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Condition
Start by recalling that covering the 'awrah is a condition (shart) for salah. If this condition is violated, salah becomes invalid.
2
Recognize the Scenario
The passage addresses a case where 'awrah is exposed from multiple, separate spots (tafarruq al-inkishaf)—e.g., due to a tear in clothing.
3
Apply Cumulative Measurement
Instead of treating each spot individually, sum the total exposed area. Do not require a single continuous exposure of a quarter.
This is an extension of the single-spot rule by analogy (qiyas).
4
Determine the Threshold
Compare the total to a quarter of the smallest exposed limb (asghar al-a'da' al-munkashifa). The smallest limb is chosen as the benchmark for leniency.
For example, if the exposed spots are on arm, thigh, and abdomen, the smallest limb might be the forearm.
5
State the Ruling
If the total area reaches or exceeds that quarter, salah is invalid (fasid). If below, the prayer remains valid.
This ruling is based on juristic reasoning; no direct hadith or companion saying is found.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳۸۳) ولو تفرق الانكشاف على اعضاء من العورة وكان جملة ما تفرق يبلغ ربع اصغر الاعضاء المنكشفة منع والا فلا.
ترجمه : (۳۸۳) اور اگر ستر عورت کے اعضاء میں سے مختلف جگہ سے کھل گیا اور جتنا کھلا اس کا مجموعہ کھلے ہوئے اعضاء میں سے چھوٹے عضو کی چوتھائی کو پہنچ جائے تو نماز جائز نہیں ہوگی ، اور چوتھائی سے کم ہو تو جائز ہوگی۔
تشریح : ایک جگہ سے چوتھائی عضو نہیں کھلا ہے، بلکہ پھٹن کی وجہ سے مختلف جگہ سے ستر عورت کی جگہ کھلی ہے، اور سب کو ملایا جائے تو ستر عورت کی جو چھوٹی جگہ ہے اس کی چوتھائی کو پہنچ جاتی ہو تو نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی ، اور چوتھائی سے کم ہو تو نماز فاسد نہیں ہوگی ۔ اس کے لئے کوئی حدیث یا قول صحابی نہیں ملا۔
(383) And if the exposure is scattered over (different) limbs of the 'awrah, and the total of what is exposed reaches a quarter of the smallest of the exposed limbs, it prevents (validity), otherwise not. Translation: If the 'awrah is exposed from different places, and the total of what is exposed reaches a quarter of the smallest limb among those exposed, then the prayer is not valid; if it is less than a quarter, then it will be valid. Commentary: It is not that a quarter of a limb is exposed from one place, but due to a tear, the 'awrah is exposed from multiple places. If, when combined, it reaches a quarter of the smallest part of the 'awrah, then the prayer becomes invalid; if less than a quarter, the prayer does not become invalid. No hadith or saying of a companion has been found for this.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement concerning exposure of the 'awrah from multiple locations. The author states that if the 'awrah is exposed from different spots, and the total area of exposure, when combined, equals a quarter of the smallest limb among the exposed parts, then the prayer becomes invalid. If the total is less than a quarter, the prayer remains valid. The commentary notes that this ruling is based on the general principle of 'kathir' (significant amount) applied to scattered exposure. Importantly, the author acknowledges that no direct hadith or companion saying is found for this specific scenario; it is derived by analogy (qiyas) from the ruling on a single spot exposure. In Hanafi fiqh, this is an extension of the same principle: the total exposed area is considered cumulatively. This demonstrates the use of juristic reasoning (ijtihad) where textual evidence is absent.

Key Terms
تفرق الانكشاف (tafarruq al-inkishaf): Exposure of the 'awrah from multiple separate locations.
اصغر الاعضاء (asghar al-a'da'): The smallest limb among the exposed parts of the 'awrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The prayer is valid because no single spot is a quarter

Key Takeaway
Scattered exposure of 'awrah is cumulatively measured; if the total area equals or exceeds a quarter of the smallest exposed limb, salah is invalid.

Qiblah Dispensation for Incapacity
Ruling on facing qiblah with excuses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on facing the qiblah when unable, identify the three valid excuses, and explain the Quranic proof from Surah Al-Baqarah 2:115.

Core Idea
Incapacity to face the qiblah due to illness or fear makes any safe direction valid.

This passage addresses a practical concession in prayer: when a person cannot face the qiblah due to genuine reasons, the requirement is lifted. The Hanafi school derives this from a Quranic verse affirming Allah's omnipresence. Understanding this dispensation prevents unnecessary hardship while preserving the prayer's validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? Facing the qiblah during prayer. The default ruling is that it is wajib (obligatory). The passage discusses exceptions when a person is unable.
The default ruling is not explicitly stated but understood from the context.
2
List the excuses that permit deviation
From the text: illness, inability to dismount from an animal (or by extension a vehicle), and fear of an enemy. These create a genuine incapacity (ajz).
The Arabic uses 'او' (or) to list the excuses.
3
Locate the dalil
The author cites Quran 2:115: 'To Allah belongs the east and the west. So wherever you turn, there is the face of Allah.' This verse is the primary proof.
The verse is quoted in Arabic in the passage.
4
Analyze wajh al-dalalah
The verse indicates Allah's omnipresence; the phrase 'there is the face of Allah' shows that any direction is acceptable when facing the qiblah is impossible. The imperative 'tawallaw' (you turn) implies permission.
Hanafi usul: a command (amr) indicates obligation, but here it is interpreted as permission due to the context of incapacity.
5
Note the mufta bihi implication
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that a person unable to face the qiblah due to these excuses may pray in whichever direction they can, and the prayer is valid.
There is no dispute within the Hanafi school on this point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳۸۴) ومن عجز عن استقبال القبلة لمرض او [نزوله عن الدابة او خوف عدو] 
ترجمه : (۳۸۴) اور جو مرض کے سبب، یا چوپائے سے نیچے اترنے سے استقبال قبلہ سے عاجز ہو جائے ، یادشمن کے خوف کی وجہ سے قبلہ کی طرف منھ نہ کر سکے تو جس جانب قدرت ہو اور امن ہو وہ اس کا قبلہ ہے۔
تشریح : اصل تو یہ ہے کہ قبلہ کی طرف توجہ کرے، [1] لیکن بیماری کی وجہ سے قبلے کی طرف توجہ نہیں کر سکتا ہے، [۲] یا چوپائے پر یاریل پر یا ہوائی جہاز پر سوار ہے اور اس سے اترنے سے عاجز ہے، یاریل پر یا ہوائی جہاز پر قبلے کی طرف توجہ کر کے نماز پڑھنے سے عاجز ہے [۳] یادشمن کا خوف ہے جسکی وجہ سے قبلے کی طرف توجہ کرنا مشکل ہے تو جدھر توجہ کر سکتا ہو وہی اس کا قبلہ ہے اور اسی طرف توجہ کر کے نماز پڑھنے سے نماز ہو جائے گی۔
وجه : (۱) اس کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے ۔ ولله المشرق والمغرب فاينما تولوا فثم وجه الله _ ( آیت۱۵ا،سورة البقرة)
(384) And whoever is unable to face the qiblah due to illness or [dismounting from an animal or fear of an enemy]. Translation: And if a person is unable to face the qiblah due to illness, or due to dismounting from an animal, or cannot face the qiblah because of fear of an enemy, then whatever direction he is able to face and is safe, that is his qiblah. Commentary: The origin is that one should face the qiblah, [1] but if due to illness he cannot turn towards the qiblah, [2] or he is riding on an animal, or on a train, or on an airplane and is unable to dismount, or is unable to pray facing the qiblah on the train or airplane, [3] or there is fear of an enemy making it difficult to face the qiblah, then whichever direction he is able to face, that is his qiblah, and by praying facing that direction, the prayer will be valid. Proof: (1) The evidence for this is the verse: 'And to Allah belongs the east and the west. So wherever you [may] turn, there is the face of Allah.' (Surah Al-Baqarah 2:115)
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the dispensation in facing the qiblah for prayer. The author states that if a person is unable to face the qiblah due to illness, while riding and unable to dismount, or due to fear of an enemy, then they may pray in any direction they can face safely. The commentary clarifies that the default obligation is to face the qiblah, but these excuses allow deviation. The proof is the Quranic verse that emphasizes Allah's omnipresence, indicating that direction is not absolute when there is genuine incapacity. In Hanafi fiqh, this is consistent with the principle of necessity (darurah) overriding normal requirements. The ruling applies to both obligatory and supererogatory prayers, but for obligatory prayers, one must strive to face the qiblah as much as possible. However, if completely unable, the prayer is valid in any direction.

Key Terms
استقبال القبلة (istiqbal al-qiblah): Facing the direction of the Kaaba during prayer.
عجز (ajz): Inability to perform an obligatory act, excusing the requirement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Being in a moving train and unable to face the qiblah
B) Forgetting the direction of the qiblah
C) Liking a different direction
D) Being in a hurry

Key Takeaway
When facing the qiblah is genuinely impossible due to illness, travel constraints, or fear, prayer in any direction is valid.

The Hanafi Ruling on Qibla When Uncertain: Taharrī Substitutes
Ruling with proof on qibla in constraint and uncertainty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qibla when uncertain and explain why taharrī substitutes for the actual qibla, using the proofs cited.

Core Idea
When qibla is uncertain, taharrī becomes the actual qibla—no repetition needed if mistaken.

This passage addresses a common practical scenario: what if you cannot determine the direction of the Ka'ba? The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling based on the principle that genuine effort (taharrī) replaces the requirement of facing the exact qibla. Through Quranic verse, hadith, and logical reasoning, the school establishes that such a prayer is valid and does not require repetition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Scenarios
The passage covers two situations: (1) when one is unable to dismount or fears an enemy, and (2) when the qibla is uncertain. State the ruling for each.
The first scenario is about physical constraint; the second is about ignorance of direction.
2
Locate the Proofs (Dalil)
Find the Quranic verse (2:115) and two hadith cited: the hadith of Ibn 'Umar on fear prayer and the hadith of Jabir on taharrī in the cloud.
The hadith of Jabir is the primary proof for the taharrī ruling.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
For each proof, identify the specific phrase that indicates validity. For example, the Prophet's statement 'قد أجزأت صلواتكم' directly shows no repetition.
Focus on how the proof is used to derive the ruling.
4
Note the Cross-Madhhab Dispute
The Shafi'i school holds that if the correct direction is later discovered, the prayer must be repeated. Contrast with the Hanafi position.
The disagreement stems from different views on whether taharrī substitutes or merely guides.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi Tarjih
Explain why the Hanafi school relies on the hadith and the principle 'taharrī is the actual qibla' to support the ruling.
The Hanafi position is considered the mufta bihi.

فصل في القبلة عجز عن النزول عن دابته او خاف عدوا فقبلته جهة قدرته وامنه (۳۸۵) ومن اشتبهت عليه القبلة البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ مجبوری کے موقع پر کسی اور طرف توجہ کر کے نماز پڑھ لی تو نماز ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ وہاں اللہ کا چہرہ ہے۔ (۲) اس اثر میں ہے۔ ان عبد الله بن عمر كان اذا سئل عن صلوة الخوف قال .... فان كان خوف هو اشد من ذالک صلوا رجالا قياما على اقدامهم ، أو ركبانا مستقبلى القبلة أو غير مستقبليها ۔(بخاری شریف، کتاب التفسیر ، باب قولہ فان خفتم فرجالا اور کہانا ص اے کے نمبر ۴۵۳۵) اس اثر میں ہے کہ خوف زیادہ ہو تو قبلہ کے علاوہ کی طرف بھی نماز پڑھے گا تو نماز جائز ہو جائے گی۔ : جهة قدرته : جس جانب قدرت ہو اسی جانب توجہ کر لے۔ ترجمه : (۳۸۵) اور جس پر قبلہ مشتبہ ہو جائے اور وہاں کوئی خبر دینے والا نہ ہو اور محراب بھی نہ ہو تو تحری کر کے نماز پڑھے ۔ اور اگر خطا کرے تب بھی اس پر اعادہ نہیں۔ تشریح : یہاں پانچ مسلے اس اصول پر مبنی ہیں کہ قبلہ مشتبہ ہو جائے تو تحری اصل قبلہ بن جاتی ہے۔ کسی کوقبلہ معلوم نہ ہو اور وہاں کوئی خبر دینے والا بھی نہ ہو، اور کوئی محراب یا علامت بھی نہ ہو جس سے قبلے کا اندازہ لگے تو تحری اصل ہو جاتی ہے، پس اگر تحری کرے اور نماز پڑھ لی تو نماز ہو جائے گی چاہے بعد میں پتہ لگے کہ قبلہ میں غلطی ہوگئی ، کیونکہ تحری اصل تھی جو کر لی۔ صلى الله وجه : (۱) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن جابر قال كنا مع النبي عله في مسير او سرية فاصابنا غيم فتحرينا واختلفنا في القبلة فصلى كل رجل منا على حدة فجعل احدنا يخط بين يديه لنعلم امكنتنا فلما اصبحنا نظرناه فاذا تھی ، باب نحن قد صلينا على غير القبلة فذكرنا ذلك للنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال قد اجزأت صلواتكم - (سنل للبيهقی ، با الاختلاف في القبلة عند التحری، ج ثانی، ص ۱۶ نمبر ۲۲۳۵ ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء فی الرجل یصلی الغير القبلة في الغيم ص ۹۴ نمبر ۳۴۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ تحری کر کے نماز پڑھی تو قبلہ غلط بھی ہو جائے تو نماز لوٹانے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ تحری ہی اس کا قبلہ ہو گیا۔ (۲) عن عبد الله بن عامر بن ربيعة عن أبيه قال : كنا مع النبي الله في سفر في ليلة صلى الله مظلمة ، فلم ندر أين القبلة فصلى كل رجل منا على حياله ، فلما أصبحنا ذكرنا ذالك للنبی علم فنزل : فأينما تولوا فثم وجه الله ) آیت ۱۱۵، سورۃ البقرۃ ۲ ) ( ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء في الرجل يصلى لغير القبلة في الغيم ص ۱۹۴، نمبر ۳۴۵ رابن ماجہ شریف ، باب من یصلی لغیر القبلة وصولا یعلم ، ص ۱۴۳، نمبر ۱۰۲۰) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ غیر قبلہ کی طرف نماز پڑھی اور ہو بھی گئی۔ اصول : قبلہ مشتبہ ہوتے وقت تحری قبلہ ہے۔
Section on the qibla. One who is unable to dismount from his animal or fears an enemy, his qibla is the direction of his ability and safety. (385) And one for whom the qibla is uncertain, he performs taharrī and there is no repetition upon him if he errs. Explanation:... Principle: When the qibla is uncertain, taharrī is the actual qibla.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It opens the section on qibla with two scenarios: first, when one cannot dismount or fears an enemy, he prays as best he can, facing whatever direction he safely can. The Hanafi position is that necessity overrides the requirement of facing the Ka'ba, and the prayer is valid. Second, when the qibla is genuinely unknown (no informant, no mihrāb, no sign), one performs ijtihad (taharrī) and prays; even if mistaken, no repetition is required because taharrī becomes the effective qibla. The author cites three proofs: (1) the Quranic verse 'Wherever you turn, there is the face of Allah' (2:115), indicating that in constraint any direction suffices. (2) The hadith of Ibn 'Umar on the prayer of fear, allowing prayer in any direction when danger is severe. (3) The hadith of Jābir and the cloud, where the companions performed taharrī and prayed in different directions, and the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) confirmed their prayer was valid. The principle established: taharrī substitutes for the actual qibla when it is unknown.

Key Terms
قبلة (qibla): The direction of the Ka'ba in Makkah, which must be faced during prayer.
تحري (taharrī): The act of striving to determine the correct direction of qibla through ijtihad based on available signs or reasoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if someone performs taharrī for qibla but later finds out he was facing the wrong direction?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid and no repetition is needed.
C) Only the first rak'ah is valid, the rest must be repeated.
D) The prayer is valid only if he had no other option.

Key Takeaway
When qibla is unknown, performing taharrī (diligent effort) makes the prayer valid even if the direction was incorrect, because taharrī becomes the effective qibla.

Ruling on Qibla Correction During Prayer
Ruling with proof: qibla correction mid-prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when one realizes a qibla mistake during prayer and explain the proof from the hadith of the change of qibla.

Core Idea
Realizing qibla mistake in prayer? Turn and continue — the prayer remains valid.

Imagine you have performed taharrī and begun praying, only to discover mid-prayer that you were facing the wrong direction. What should you do? The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling based on a prophetic precedent. This lesson will guide you through the ruling and its proof, showing that corrective turning does not break the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and its Ruling
The act in question is turning one's body during prayer to face the correct qibla after realizing a mistake. The ruling: the prayer remains valid (sahih) and the person continues from where he left off. There is no need to restart.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Locate the Dalil
The proof is the hadith of 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar (Bukhari) when the qibla command changed from Jerusalem to the Ka'ba. The companions at Quba' turned mid-prayer without restarting.
Hadith is sahih and mutawatir in meaning.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The companions' action shows that turning is permissible and does not invalidate the prayer. The Prophet (ﷺ) did not order them to repeat, indicating that the prayer was valid.
The operative phrase: فاستداروا إلى الكعبة.
4
Apply the Principle
The Hanafi principle: taharrī (endeavor) establishes the qibla for that prayer. Once the true qibla becomes known, one must face it. The prayer is built on the initial valid intention.
This aligns with the maxim: 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha'.
5
Note the Consequence
If the mistake is realized after the prayer, the prayer is valid and no repetition is needed (assuming taharrī was performed). If no taharrī was done, the prayer is invalid.
This is an important distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳۸۶) وان علم بخطئه في صلوته استدار وبنى ترجمه : (۳۸۶) اور اگر اپنی غلطی کونماز میں ہی جانا تو گھوم جائے اور بنا کرے۔ تشریح : [۲] تحری کر کے نماز شروع کی تھی اور قبلے کی غلطی نماز کے درمیان میں پتہ چلا تو اسی درمیان قبلے کی طرف گھوم جائے اور نماز کی بنا کر لے نماز کو دہرانے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ تحری ہی قبلہ بن گیا وجه : (۱) اس حديث میں ہے۔ عن عبدالله بن عمر قال : بينا الناس بقباء في صلاة الصبح اذ جائهم آت فقال : ان رسول الله علم قد انزل عليه الليلة قرآن ، قدأمر أن يستقبل الكعبة ، فاستقبلوها ، و كانت وجوههم الى الشام فاستداروا الى الكعبة - ( بخاری شریف، باب ما جاء فی القبلة ، الخ، ص ۵۷، نمبر ۴۰۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ نماز میں قبلہ کی طرف گھوم گئے ۔
(386) And if he knows his mistake during his prayer, he turns around and builds (i.e., continues his prayer). Translation: (386) And if he realizes his mistake in prayer itself, then he turns and builds. Explanation: He had started prayer with taharrī and realized the qibla error during prayer; he turns toward the qibla and continues, no need to repeat. Proof: Hadith of Ibn 'Umar that when the command to face the Ka'ba came, the people at Quba' turned in their prayer.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage gives a ruling with proof concerning the situation where a person has performed taharrī and is in prayer, then discovers that he was facing the wrong direction. The Hanafi position is that he should immediately turn to the correct qibla and continue his prayer from where he left off; there is no need to restart. The proof is the well-known incident when the qibla was changed from Jerusalem to the Ka'ba: the people at Quba' were praying towards Jerusalem when a messenger came informing them of the change, and they turned towards the Ka'ba in the middle of the prayer. This shows that turning is permitted and does not invalidate the prayer. The principle: since taharrī served as the qibla at the start, the prayer is valid until the correct direction becomes known, and then one must face it.

Key Terms
استدار (istadāra): To turn around, specifically turning one's body during prayer to face the qibla.
بنا (banā): To build upon, i.e., continue the prayer from where one left off rather than starting anew.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should a person do if they realize they are facing the wrong qibla during prayer?
A) Stop the prayer and repeat it from the beginning.
B) Turn to the correct qibla and continue the prayer.
C) Finish the prayer as is, since it is valid.
D) Perform a prostration of forgetfulness (sajdah al-sahw) and then continue.

Key Takeaway
If you realize a qibla mistake during prayer after making taharrī, turn to the correct direction and continue; the prayer is valid and need not be repeated.

Ruling on Knowing Correct Qibla During Prayer Without Taharrī
Ruling: if one knows he is correct during prayer without taharrī, it becomes invalid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a person prays without taharrī and learns the correct qibla during the prayer, and explain why it invalidates the prayer.

Core Idea
Without taharrī, knowing you are correct during prayer invalidates it.

This lesson covers a scenario from the chapter on qibla: a person prays without first performing taharrī (effort to determine the qibla). If during the prayer he becomes certain he is facing the correct direction, or even that he missed it, the prayer becomes invalid (fasid). The rationale is that taharrī was a required preliminary effort; its omission cannot be compensated by accidental correctness unless that correctness is confirmed only after the prayer is complete.

Guided Path
1
Identify the omission
The person omitted taharrī before starting the prayer. Taharrī is required when the qibla direction is uncertain.
Taharrī is a wajib in the Hanafi school for one who is uncertain of the qibla.
2
Identify the time of knowledge
The person becomes certain about the qibla direction during the prayer, not after completion.
This is the key difference from the previous case where certainty after prayer validates.
3
Apply the principle
Without taharrī, the prayer is only valid if the actual qibla facing is confirmed after the prayer. Knowledge during prayer does not remedy the missing taharrī.
The act of taharrī is a condition (shart) that cannot be replaced by mid-prayer discovery.
4
State the ruling
The prayer becomes fasid (invalid) and must be repeated.
Fasid means invalid but with a legal nuance; repetition is required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳۸۸) وان علم باصابته فيها فسدت كما لو لم يعلم اصابته اصلا ترجمه : (۳۸۸) اور اگر صیح ہونا نماز کے اندر معلوم ہوا تو نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی جیسا کہ صحیح ہونے کا بالکل پتہ نہیں چلا ۔ تشریح : [۴) تحری کئے بغیر نماز پڑھی اور درمیان نماز میں معلوم ہوا کہ قبلے کی جانب رخ نہیں ہے تو نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی ، کیونکہ یہاں تحری اصل تھی وہ بھی نہیں ہوئی ، اور قبلے کی طرف رخ کرنا چاہئے تھا وہ بھی نہیں ہوا اس لئے نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی، [۵] پانچویں صورت یہ ہے کہ نماز کے بعد بھی معلوم نہیں ہوا کہ قبلے کی طرف رخ تھا یا اس کے خلاف میں تھا تب بھی نماز فاسد ہوگی ،اس لئے کہ تحری بھی نہیں کی ، اور قبلے کی طرف ہونا بھی یقینی نہیں ہے۔
(388) And if he knows his correctness in it, it becomes invalid, just as if he had not known his correctness at all. Translation: (388) And if he knows the correctness during the prayer, the prayer becomes invalid, as if he had not known the correctness at all. Explanation: [4] He prayed without taharrī and during prayer he knew that he was not facing the qibla, so the prayer is invalid, because here taharrī was the original (required) which was not done, and facing the qibla was also not done. [5] The fifth situation is that even after prayer he did not know whether he was facing the qibla or opposite; here also the prayer is invalid, because he did not do taharrī and facing the qibla is not certain.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This ruling covers two scenarios (the fourth and fifth of the five issues). The fourth: a person prays without taharrī and during the prayer realizes he is not facing the qibla. The prayer becomes invalid (fasid). The fifth: a person prays without taharrī and after prayer is uncertain whether he faced the qibla or not. Here also the prayer is invalid. The reason in both cases is that taharrī was required but omitted, and the actual qibla was either known to be missed or not confirmed. Since neither taharrī nor actual facing of the qibla is established, the prayer cannot be valid. This highlights that taharrī is a substitute for the actual qibla when unknown; without it, the prayer is only valid if the actual qibla was faced and known after completion (as in the previous ruling), but if known during prayer or never known, it is invalid.

Key Terms
فاسد (fāsid): Invalid; the prayer must be repeated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a person prays without taharrī and during the prayer realizes he is facing the wrong direction?
A) He should turn and continue; the prayer is valid.
B) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
C) He should continue and perform sajdah al-sahw at the end.
D) The prayer is valid if he faces the correct direction after turning.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, performing taharrī is essential when the qibla is uncertain; without it, only certainty after prayer can validate it, not knowledge during prayer.

Ruling on a Group Performing Taharrī in Different Directions
Ruling with rational proof on validity of following imam with unknown qibla

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on congregational prayer when the imam's qibla direction is unknown and explain the rational basis for it.

Core Idea
Following an imam remains valid as long as the follower does not hold a positive belief that the imam is in error.

This lesson examines a specific scenario where a congregation performs individual taharrī in darkness, each facing a different direction, and they are ignorant of the imam's qibla. The Hanafi school rules their prayer valid, a decision rooted in a key principle about the nature of following (ittibā'). We will unpack this principle and its proof, and see how ignorance of error preserves the validity of the congregation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Read the passage carefully. Note the setting: darkness, a group performs taharrī (individual effort to determine qibla), each believer prays in a different direction, and they are following an imam whose direction they do not know.
The key is that they are ignorant of the imam's qibla, not that they know it is wrong.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The passage clearly states that the prayer of all followers is valid (sahih). No distinction is made between those who may have guessed correctly and those who guessed differently.
The ruling is unanimous in the Hanafi school on this point.
3
Understand the underlying principle
The validity of ittibā' (following the imam) depends on the follower's state of mind. If the follower believes the imam is in error, then he has not truly followed him, and his prayer is invalid. If he is ignorant of any error, his following is valid.
This is a rational (dalil aqli) proof based on the definition of following.
4
Apply the principle to the scenario
Since the followers in the scenario do not know the imam's direction, they have no belief that he is wrong. Therefore, their ittibā' is correct, and their prayer is valid. The possibility that the imam might actually be facing a wrong direction does not affect the ruling because the followers lack certain knowledge.
Contrast with the case where a follower knows the imam is wrong – then the prayer would be invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳۸۹) ولو تحرى قوم جهات وجهلوا حال امامهم ترجمه : (۳۸۹) ایک قوم نے مختلف جہت کی تحری کی اور امام کا حال معلوم نہیں ہے تو نماز جائز ہو جائے گی۔ تشریح : یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ اعتقاد ہو کہ امام غلط رخ پر ہے تو اس کی اتباع ہی نہیں ہوئی اس لئے نماز نہیں ہوگی ، اور اگر اس کا حال ہی معلوم نہ ہو اس لئے اس کے بارے میں غلط ہونے کا اعتقاد نہ ہو اس لئے اس کی اتباع صحیح ہوئی اس لئے مقتدی کی نماز درست ہو جائے گی ۔ صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اندھیرے میں کچھ لوگوں نے مل کر تحری کی اور مختلف جہت میں نماز پڑھی ، اور ان کو معلوم نہیں تھا کہ امام کس رخ پر ہے تو سب کی نماز درست ہو جائے گی۔ وجه : (۱) امام کا حال معلوم نہیں ہے اس لئے غلط ہونے کا اعتقاد نہیں ہے اس لئے اتباع درست ہوئی اس لئے نماز درست
(389) And if a group perform taharrī in different directions and they are ignorant of the state of their imam. Translation: (389) A group performed taharrī in different directions and the state of the imam is not known, then the prayer is permissible (valid). Explanation: This issue is based on the principle that if one believes the imam is on the wrong direction, then he has not followed him, so the prayer is not valid; but if his state is simply unknown, there is no belief that he is wrong, so his following is correct and the follower's prayer is valid. The scenario: in darkness, some people collectively performed taharrī and prayed in different directions, and they did not know which direction the imam faced, then all their prayers are valid. Proof: The imam's state is unknown, so there is no belief that he is wrong, thus following is correct and prayer is valid.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with rational proof (istihsan principle). It addresses a situation where a group of people perform individual taharrī in darkness and each prays in a different direction, but they are following an imam whose qibla direction they do not know. The Hanafi ruling is that their prayer is valid. The reasoning: validity of following an imam depends on the follower not believing the imam is in error. Since the direction is unknown, there is no positive belief of error, so the following is valid. Conversely, if one knows the imam is facing the wrong direction, following him would invalidate the prayer. This is a qiyas-based ruling (dalil aqli).

Key Terms
اتباع (ittibā'): Following the imam in prayer; the act of conforming to the imam's actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a group prays in congregation, each having performed taharrī in different directions, and they do not know the direction of the imam?
A) The prayer of the followers is invalid because they are not all facing the same direction.
B) The prayer is valid for those who happen to face the same direction as the imam.
C) The prayer of all followers is valid because they do not believe the imam is in error.
D) The prayer is invalid because taharrī must be unanimous.

Key Takeaway
When the follower does not believe the imam is in error, the ittibā' is valid, and thus the prayer is valid even if the imam's direction is unknown.

Turning to the Qibla After Taharrī
Ruling on turning towards qibla when error discovered during prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for each scenario of qibla error during prayer and apply the hadith proof to justify turning during prayer.

Core Idea
After taharrī, an error in qibla does not invalidate prayer—turn and build upon it, like the Companions did.

This lesson examines the Hanafi rulings on what happens when a person realizes during prayer that he was facing the wrong qibla direction, particularly after performing ijtihad (taharrī). The passage from the matn presents four scenarios, each with a distinct ruling, supported by the famous hadith of the Companions at Quba'. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for knowing when a prayer must be repeated and when it remains valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenarios
The passage presents four situations based on whether ijtihad was performed and when the error or correctness is discovered. Extract each scenario clearly.
Scenarios 386-389, plus the group case.
2
Extract the ruling for each
For each scenario, determine whether the prayer is sahih or fasid, and note any required action (e.g., turning).
Focus on the conditions that affect validity.
3
Analyze the proof
The hadith of Ibn Umar is cited for scenario 387. Understand how the Companions' action proves that turning during prayer without restarting is permissible.
The proof is that they turned and continued, not that they repeated.
4
Apply the principle
The underlying principle is that taharrī substitutes for actual knowledge. If ijtihad was done, the prayer is valid even if direction wrong. If no ijtihad, validity depends on factual correctness.
This explains why scenario 389 is invalid.

ولم يكن عنده مخبر ولا محراب تحرى ولا اعادة عليه لو اخطأ (٣٨٦) وان علم بخطئه في صلوته استدار وبنى (٣٨٧) وان شرع بلا تحر فعلم بعد فراغه انه اصاب صحت (٣٨٨) وان علم باصابته فيها فسدت كما لو لم يعلم اصابته اصلا (٣٨٩) ولو تحرى قوم جهات وجهلوا حال امامهم

Chapter on Qibla. If one has no informant and no mihrab, he performs ijtihad and there is no repetition upon him if he errs (386). And if he knows his error in his prayer, he turns and builds upon it (387). And if he begins without ijtihad and knows after finishing that he was correct, it is valid (388). And if he knows his correctness during it, it is invalid, just as if he did not know his correctness at all (389). And if a group performs ijtihad in different directions and they are ignorant of the situation of their imam.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage presents rulings related to ijtihad (taharrī) for the qibla direction. The first ruling (386) states that a person who has no means of knowing the qibla (no informant or mihrab) must perform ijtihad, and if he errs, he is not required to repeat the prayer (since he did his best). The second ruling (387) addresses a situation where one performed ijtihad but discovers during the prayer that he was facing the wrong direction; he must turn to the correct qibla and continue his prayer, building upon what has been done. The proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar about the people of Quba' turning towards the Kaaba during prayer when the revelation came. The commentator explains that the ijtihad itself becomes the qibla (for validity). The third ruling (388) says if one starts without ijtihad and later, after finishing, knows he faced the correct direction, the prayer is valid because he happened to face the qibla. The fourth (389) says if he knows during the prayer that he is correct, the prayer becomes invalid (because he now has certainty but didn't base his action on ijtihad). The final statement introduces a scenario where a group performs ijtihad in different directions and are unaware of the imam's direction; the ruling that follows (on next page) is that their prayers are valid.

Key Terms
تحري (taharrī): Ijtihad or exertion to determine the qibla direction when it is not known.
قبلة (qibla): The direction of the Kaaba in Mecca, which must be faced during prayer.
استدارة (istidāra): Turning around to face the correct direction during prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person performs ijtihad (taharrī) for qibla and then realizes during prayer that he was facing the wrong direction, what should he do?
A) Stop the prayer and start over.
B) Turn to the correct qibla and continue the prayer from where he was.
C) Complete the prayer as is and repeat it later.
D) Perform a sajda al-sahw and then turn.

Key Takeaway
After performing ijtihad for qibla, a mistaken direction does not invalidate the prayer; one turns to the correct direction and continues building upon the prayer.

Valid Prayer Without Ijtihad if Qibla Was Correct
Ruling on validity when ijtihad is omitted but qibla is correct

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a prayer performed without ijtihad when the correct qibla direction is later confirmed.

Core Idea
Facing the qibla in reality, not merely searching for it, determines validity.

This lesson examines a specific case: a person begins prayer without effort to find the qibla (taharrī), but after finishing discovers they were facing the correct direction. The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling that prioritizes the actual fulfillment of the condition over the method used. Understanding this distinction helps avoid unnecessary invalidation of prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its essential condition
The act is prayer (salah). The key condition for validity is facing the qibla. Identify which conditions are essential and which are procedural means.
Taharrī (ijtihad) is a means to find qibla, not a condition of validity.
2
Distinguish between means and condition
Clarify that ijtihad (taharrī) is a recommended or obligatory step when direction is unknown, but it is not a pillar or condition. The actual requirement is facing the Kaaba.
Hanafi: if one faces qibla correctly, the condition is met regardless of ijtihad.
3
Apply the ruling to the given scenario
Take the scenario: person starts prayer without ijtihad, later finds direction was correct. Apply the principle: condition (qibla direction) was satisfied, so prayer is valid.
Contrast with scenario where direction was wrong: prayer would be invalid.
4
Note cross-madhhab consideration
Some schools hold that ijtihad is a condition for validity when qibla is uncertain. The Hanafi position is more lenient: actual direction suffices.
This is a point of legitimate ikhtilaf.

That he began prayer without ijtihad. And after finishing the prayer it became known that he was in the correct direction, so the prayer is correct, because even though there was no ijtihad, he was facing the qibla, so the prayer is valid.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling for a person who started his prayer without performing any ijtihad (taharrī) to determine the qibla. After completing the prayer, he discovers that he happened to be facing the correct direction (the Kaaba). According to the Hanafi school, his prayer is valid. The reason is that the essential condition for the validity of prayer is facing the qibla, and that condition was fulfilled, even though he did not perform ijtihad. Ijtihad is only required when the direction is unknown; here, by chance, he faced correctly, so the prayer is accepted.

Key Terms
تحري (taharrī): Ijtihad to find qibla direction.

D) The prayer is invalid because he omitted ijtihad.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a prayer is valid if the qibla direction was actually faced, even if no ijtihad was performed to find it.

Validity of Prayer When Congregation Differs in Qibla
Ruling on a group praying in different directions after ijtihad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a group's prayer when they differ in qibla after ijtihad and apply the principle of ittibāʿ based on ignorance of the imam's error.

Core Idea
Following an imam is valid unless you believe him wrong; ignorance of error suffices for validity.

Imagine praying in darkness with a group, each person trying to find the qibla by ijtihad, and everyone ends up facing different directions, including the imam. Is your prayer valid? The Hanafi school says yes, based on a powerful hadith and a clear principle about what it means to 'follow' an imam. This lesson unpacks that ruling and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
First, read the passage and state the overall Hanafi ruling: What happens to the prayers of followers who prayed in different directions after ijtihad, not knowing the imam's direction?
2
Extract the Core Principle
The commentator gives a key principle: validity of following (ittibāʿ) depends on the follower's belief about the imam. What is that principle? When is ittibāʿ valid or invalid?
Look for the phrase 'امام کے بارے میں غلط ہونے کا اعتقاد' in the Urdu text.
3
Examine the Dalil
The passage cites a hadith of Jabir (RA). Read the hadith and identify how it supports the ruling. What did the Prophet say when the Companions realised they had prayed facing the wrong direction?
The hadith is narrated by Bayhaqi and Tirmidhi.
4
Apply the Principle to the Scenario
Put the principle together with the scenario. The followers did not know the imam's direction, so they had no belief he was wrong. Therefore their following was valid, and their prayers are valid.
Contrast with: if they had believed the imam was wrong, their prayers would be invalid.

اصول : امام کے بارے میں غلط ہونے کا اعتقاد ہو تو اس کی اتباع صحیح نہیں ہے اور نماز بھی نهیں ہوگی۔
Translation: (389) A group performed ijtihad in different directions and they are ignorant of the situation of their imam, then the prayer is permissible. Explanation: This issue is based on the principle that if one believes the imam is in a wrong direction, then his following (of the imam) did not occur, so the prayer is not valid. But if his situation is not known, then there is no belief of him being wrong, so his following is correct, and the follower's prayer is valid. The scenario: In darkness, some people together performed ijtihad and prayed in different directions, and they did not know which direction the imam faced, so all their prayers are valid. Reasons: (1) The imam's situation is unknown, so there is no belief of error, thus following is correct and prayer valid. (2) The second reason is that ijtihad was the origin and they did it, so also prayer is valid. (3) The hadith: Jabir said: We were with the Prophet on a journey or expedition, clouds covered us, we did ijtihad and differed in qibla, each of us prayed individually, one would draw a line before him so we could know our places. When morning came, we looked and we had prayed towards other than the qibla. We mentioned that to the Prophet, and he said: 'Your prayers are sufficient.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Tirmidhi) Principle: If one believes the imam is wrong, his following is not correct and the prayer is not valid.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage addresses a scenario where a group of people in darkness perform ijtihad individually to determine the qibla, and each prays in a different direction (likely as followers of an imam whose direction they do not know). The Hanafi ruling is that each person's prayer is valid. The commentator explains the underlying principle: the validity of following an imam depends on not believing the imam to be in error. If a follower is ignorant of the imam's direction, he has no belief of error, so his following is valid. Additionally, each person performed ijtihad, which suffices for personal prayer. The proof is the hadith of Jabir where the Companions differed in qibla due to clouds, and the Prophet declared their prayers valid even though they faced wrong directions. The principle derived is that certainty of the imam's error invalidates following; otherwise, it is valid.

Key Terms
اتباع (ittibāʿ): Following the imam in congregational prayer.
مقتدی (muqtadī): Follower in congregational prayer.
تحری (taḥarrī): Ijtihad to determine the qibla when it is unclear.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only those who faced correctly have valid prayer.
B) All of their prayers are valid.
C) Their prayers are invalid because they differed from the imam.
D) They must repeat the prayer after the imam.

Key Takeaway
A follower's prayer is valid if he does not believe the imam is wrong, even if he faces a different direction due to ijtihad.

Introduction to the Wajibat of Prayer (Fasl fi Wajib al-Salah)
Enumeration of wajibat of prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list at least four wajibat of prayer and explain the consequence of omitting a wajib in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, a wajib in prayer is obligatory but not a pillar — omitting it requires sajda al-sahw, not repetition.

This passage opens a new chapter on the wajibat (obligatory elements) of prayer. It states that there are eighteen wajibat in total and begins listing them. Understanding the distinction between wajib and fard is crucial for correctly applying the rules of prayer in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal category
Recognize that the passage is about wajibat. Define 'wajib' in Hanafi fiqh as an obligatory element whose omission does not invalidate the prayer but requires sajda al-sahw.
Wajib is distinct from fard (which is a pillar and omission invalidates).
2
Note the total number
The author states there are 18 wajibat. The list provided in this passage is partial (14 items appear); the full list continues in later pages.
Memorizing the 18 is common in Hanafi texts.
3
Examine the listed wajibat
Read the first few items: reciting Surah al-Fatiha, adding a surah after it, specifying recitation in first two rak'ahs, preceding Fatiha over surah, touching nose in sajda, etc.
Some items have intra-Hanafi differences; e.g., tashahhud in first sitting is wajib according to the correct narration.
4
Understand the consequence of omission
Omitting any wajib intentionally or inadvertently requires sajda al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) to compensate. The prayer remains valid.
This is the key practical difference from fard.
5
Distinguish from sunnah
Sunnah are recommended; omission does not require any compensation. Wajib are obligatory but not pillars.
This three-tier hierarchy (fard, wajib, sunnah) is characteristic of Hanafi fiqh.

This passage introduces a new chapter on the wajibat (obligatory elements) of prayer. It states that there are eighteen wajibat in total. In the Hanafi school, wajibat are obligatory elements whose omission does not invalidate the prayer but requires sajda al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) for compensation, unlike fard which are pillars.

Key Terms

The 18 Wajibat of Prayer in Hanafi Fiqh
Lists and explains the 18 wajibat of salah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the 18 wajibat of salah according to the Hanafi school, explain the Hanafi definition of wajib (distinct from fard and sunnah), and state the consequence of omission (sajdah sahw) with reference to the proofs.

Core Idea
Hanafi wajib: omission does not invalidate prayer but requires sajdah sahw.

This lesson unpacks the key Hanafi category of 'wajib' in salah, which occupies a middle ground between fard and sunnah. You will learn the 18 specific wajibat, understand why they are classified as such, and see how the school's distinctive usul leads to a different ruling than the Shafi'i school. The proofs from hadith anchor these obligations firmly in the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Hanafi hierarchy of ahkam
Recall the five categories: fard (obligatory, qati' evidence), wajib (obligatory, zanni evidence), sunnah (recommended), makruh, haram. Wajib is a distinct level: omission does not invalidate the act but requires compensation (sajdah sahw).
This distinction is unique to Hanafis.
2
Memorize the 18 wajibat listed in the source
Read through the list carefully. Note that they include recitations (Fatihah, surah), physical postures (sajdah with nose, second sajdah, ta'dil al-arkan), sittings (first sitting, tashahhud), concluding elements (salam), and specific actions for witr and 'Eid.
The list is a standard summary in Hanafi works.
3
Examine the proof for the wajib nature of ta'dil al-arkan
The hadith of the man who prayed improperly shows that the Prophet commanded him to repeat because he omitted ta'dil al-arkan. Since repetition was ordered, the omitted element must be more than sunnah—hence, wajib.
This proof establishes the obligatory nature of performing pillars with tranquility.
4
Analyze the proof for sajdah sahw upon forgetting the first sitting
The hadith of al-Mughirah instructs that if the imam stands up forgetting the first sitting, he must perform sajdah sahw. Since sajdah sahw is mandated for omission of a wajib, the first sitting is definitively wajib.
This hadith is also used to derive the rule for other wajibat.
5
Compare with the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i does not differentiate between fard and wajib; he classifies these elements as sunnah because he considers the evidence for them to be at the same level. The practical consequence is that omitting them does not require sajdah sahw in his school.
The dispute is rooted in usul al-fiqh: the definition of 'wajib' and the weight of zanni evidence.

Section on the obligations of prayer. It suffices them. Section: On the obligatory elements of prayer, and they are eighteen things. ... (then lists 18 items) ... Important note: The meaning of wajib is that it is necessary to perform it, and if it is omitted, the prayer does not become invalid, but sajdah sahw becomes necessary. And if sajdah sahw is also not performed, then the prayer is complete with disapproval (karahah). It is better to repeat that prayer, and if not repeated, the obligation is still fulfilled. In this hadith, the companion did not perform the proper completion of the pillars (ta'dil al-arkan), which was wajib, so the Prophet commanded him to repeat the prayer. ... (hadith of al-Mughirah ibn Shu'bah about sajdah sahw) ... According to Imam al-Shafi'i, there is no category of wajib; after fard it is simply sunnah, so according to him all these are sunnah.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement enumerating the 18 wajibat of prayer in the Hanafi school, followed by an explanatory note and proofs. The text first gives an earlier discussion about facing the qiblah in clouds (from page 264) but the main content is the list. The 18 wajibat are: 1) Reciting Surah al-Fatihah. 2) Reciting an additional surah in two non-specified rak'ahs of fard, and all rak'ahs of witr and nafl. 3) Specifying the recitation in the first two rak'ahs. 4) Placing al-Fatihah before the surah. 5) Touching the nose with the forehead in prostration. 6) Performing the second prostration before moving to the next action. 7) Performing all pillars with tranquility (tamani'nah). 8) The first sitting (qa'dah ula). 9) Reciting tashahhud in the first sitting (in the sound narration). 10) Reciting tashahhud in the final sitting. 11) Standing up for the third rak'ah immediately after tashahhud without delay. 12) Saying 'al-salamu 'alaykum' (not 'wa 'alaykum'). 13) Reciting qunut in witr. 14) The extra takbirs in the two 'Eid prayers. 15) Beginning every prayer with 'Allahu akbar' except the specific 'Eid prayer. 16) The takbir in the second rak'ah of 'Eid. 17) The imam reciting aloud in the first two rak'ahs of Maghrib and 'Isha. 18) Reciting silently in all rak'ahs of Zuhr and 'Asr, and the remaining rak'ahs of Maghrib and 'Isha after the first two, and in daytime nafl prayers. The note clarifies the Hanafi definition of wajib: omission does not invalidate the prayer but requires sajdah sahw; if omitted intentionally, the prayer is valid but with karahah. Proof is from the hadith of the man who prayed improperly (the 'musi' salatuh' hadith) where the omission of ta'dil al-arkan (wajib) necessitated repetition. For forgetfulness, the hadith of al-Mughirah proves sajdah sahw for forgetting the first sitting (qa'dah ula), which is wajib. Finally, the author notes the difference with Imam al-Shafi'i, who does not recognize the category of wajib at this level, considering all these as sunnah. This highlights the unique Hanafi hierarchy of ahkam.

Key Terms
واجب (wajib): An obligatory element whose omission does not invalidate the prayer but requires sajdah sahw.
سجدہ سہو (sajdah sahw): Two extra prostrations performed to compensate for an omission or addition in prayer.
تعدیل ارکان (ta'dil al-arkan): Performing the pillars of prayer with tranquility and proper posture.
قاعدہ اولی (qa'dah ula): The first sitting after two rak'ahs in a prayer of three or four rak'ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is the consequence of intentionally omitting a wajib element (like the first sitting) from the prayer without performing sajdah sahw?
A) The prayer becomes invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid but with karahah (disapproval), and it is better to repeat it.
C) The prayer is invalid and requires a fresh wudu.
D) The prayer is valid and no action is needed.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the 18 wajibat of prayer are obligatory elements whose omission does not break the prayer but necessitates sajdah sahw, distinguishing them from fard (which invalidates) and sunnah (which requires no compensation).

Definition and Consequence of Wajib in Salah
Explaining the definition and proofs of wajib in salah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of wajib in salah and identify the consequences of omitting a wajib (sajda sahw and karahah).

Core Idea
Wajib is obligatory but its omission does not invalidate prayer; sajda sahw compensates.

In this lesson, we examine the unique Hanafi category of 'wajib'. Unlike fard, which must be repeated if missed, a wajib can be compensated with sajda sahw. We will explore the definition and the evidence from hadith that establishes this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of wajib
The text states that performing a wajib is necessary (zaruri), but if omitted, the prayer does not become invalid (fasad). Instead, sajda sahw becomes binding (lazim).
This distinguishes wajib from fard, whose omission invalidates the prayer.
2
Identify consequence of omitting sajda sahw
If sajda sahw is also omitted, the prayer is complete with karahah (dislike). Repeating the prayer is better, but the obligation is still fulfilled.
This shows that wajib does not affect the validity of the prayer, only its perfection.
3
Review first hadith proof (tadelil arkan)
The hadith of the man who prayed poorly: the Prophet ordered him to repeat because he omitted tadelil arkan (ease in postures), which is wajib. This proves omission requires repetition.
The command 'ارجع فصل' indicates that the prayer was deficient due to missing a wajib.
4
Review second hadith proof (qa'da ula)
The hadith of al-Mughira: if the imam forgets the first sitting (qa'da ula) and stands, he must perform sajda sahw. Since qa'da ula is wajib, this shows that forgetting a wajib necessitates sajda sahw.
The Prophet prescribed sajda sahw specifically for this omission.
5
Synthesize the ruling
Combine the evidences: omission of a wajib necessitates sajda sahw; if sajda sahw is also omitted, prayer is valid but disliked; repeating is better.
This complete picture is the Hanafi position on wajib in salah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ضروری نوٹ : واجب کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اس کو کرنا ضروری ہے، اور وہ چھوٹ گیا تو نماز فاسد نہیں ہوگی البتہ سجدہ سہو لازِم ہوگا، اور اگر سجدہ سہو بھی نہیں کیا تو کراہیت کے ساتھ نماز پوری ہوگئی ، بہتر یہ ہے کہ اس نماز کو دوبارہ پڑھ لے، اور نہیں پڑھی تب بھی فرض ادا ہو گیا۔ اس حدیث میں صحابی نے تعدیل ارکان نہیں کی جو واجب تھی تو دوبارہ نماز پڑھنے کے لئے فرمایا۔ عن ابی ھریرة عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم دخل المسجد فدخل رجل فصلى ثم جاء فسلم على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فرد النبي عليه السلام فقال: ارجع فصل فانك لم تصل .... ثم اركع حتى تطمئن راكعا ثم ارفع حتى تعتدل قائما ، ثم اسجد حتى تطمئن ساجدا ثم ارفع حتى تطمئن جالساً ، ثم اسجد حتى تطمئن ساجدا ، ثم افعل ذالک فی صلاتک کلها - ( بخاری شریف، باب امر النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم الذی لا یتم رکوعہ بالا عادة، ص ۱۲۸، نمبر۷۹۳رابوداود شریف ، باب صلوۃ من لا یتقیم صلبه فی الرکوع ولا السجود، ص۱۳۲، نمبر ۸۵۶) اس حدیث میں تعدیل ارکان جو واجب ہے اس کو چھوڑنے پر دوبارہ نماز پڑھنے کے لئے فرمایا۔ (۲) واجب کے بھولنے میں سجدہ سہو ہے ، اسکی دلیل یہ ہے۔ عن الـمـغيــرة بن شعبة قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اذا قام الامام في الركعتين فان ذكر قبل أن يستوى قائما فليجلس ، فان استوى قائما فلا يجلس و يسجد سجدتي السهو )) ۔ (ابوداود شریف ، باب من نسی آن يتشهد وهو جالس ، ص ۱۵۷ نمبر ۱۰۳۶ر ترمذی شریف ، باب ماجاء فی سجدتي السهو قبل السلام ، ص۹۰، نمبر ۳۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ قاعدہ اولی بھول جائے تو سجدہ سہو کرے، اور قاعدہ اولی واجب ہے جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ واجب کے چھوٹنے سے سجدہ سہو واجب ہوگا۔ امام شافعی کے یہاں واجب کا درجہ نہیں ہے، فرض کے بعد سنت کا درجہ ہے اس لئے انکے یہاں یہ سب سنت کے درجے میں ہیں ۔
Essential note: The meaning of wajib is that performing it is necessary, and if it is omitted, the prayer does not become invalid; however, sajda sahw becomes binding. And if sajda sahw is also not performed, then the prayer is complete with dislike. It is better to repeat this prayer, and if not repeated, still the obligation is fulfilled. In this hadith, the companion did not perform tadelil arkan which was wajib, so the Prophet commanded him to repeat the prayer. From Abu Huraira: A man entered the mosque and prayed, then came and greeted the Prophet. The Prophet replied: 'Go back and pray, for you have not prayed... then bow until you are at ease in bowing, then rise until you are standing straight, then prostrate until you are at ease in prostration, then rise until you are at ease in sitting, then prostrate until you are at ease in prostration, then do that in all your prayers.' (Bukhari, chapter on the command of the Prophet to the one who does not complete his bowing in the usual manner, p.128, no.793; Abu Dawud, chapter on the prayer of one whose back does not straighten in bowing and prostration, p.132, no.856) In this hadith, tadelil arkan which is wajib was omitted, so he was commanded to repeat the prayer. (2) For forgetting a wajib, there is sajda sahw; its evidence is: From al-Mughira ibn Shu'ba: The Messenger of Allah said: 'When the imam stands up after two rak'ats, if he remembers before fully standing, let him sit; if he fully stands, then do not sit and perform two prostrations of forgetfulness.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on one who forgets to sit for tashahhud, p.157, no.1036; Tirmidhi, chapter on what is related about sajda sahw before salām, p.90, no.39) In this hadith, if the first sitting (qa'da ula) is forgotten, then sajda sahw is performed, and qa'da ula is wajib, so it is known that omitting a wajib makes sajda sahw obligatory. According to Imam Shafi'i, there is no category of wajib; after fard comes sunnah, so with him all these are in the level of sunnah.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (ruling_with_proof). It begins by defining the legal category of 'wajib' in the Hanafi school: it is an obligatory act whose omission does not invalidate the prayer (salah) but requires compensation via sajda sahw (prostration of forgetfulness). If sajda sahw is also omitted, the prayer remains valid but is disliked (makruh), and repeating it is recommended. The passage then provides two hadith proofs. First is the famous hadith of the man who prayed hastily (the 'musalli' who did not perform tadelil arkan—the obligation to pause in each posture). The Prophet ordered him to repeat the prayer, showing that omission of a wajib (tadelil arkan) necessitates repetition. Second is the hadith of al-Mughira concerning forgetting the first sitting (qa'da ula). If the imam forgets and stands for the third rak'ah, he must perform sajda sahw. Since qa'da ula is wajib, this hadith establishes that omission of a wajib requires sajda sahw. Finally, the passage notes an inter-madhhab difference: Imam Shafi'i does not recognize the category of 'wajib' as distinct; he considers acts that are wajib in the Hanafi school as either fard or sunnah. This has practical implications for the number of obligatory elements in prayer according to each school.

Key Terms
واجب (wajib): An obligatory act whose omission does not invalidate the prayer but requires sajda sahw; it is a distinct category between fard and sunnah.
سجدہ سہو (sajda sahw): Two prostrations performed to compensate for forgetting a wajib or for making a mistake in prayer; they do not invalidate the prayer if omitted but their omission is disliked.
تعدیل ارکان (tadelil arkan): The obligation to pause and be at ease in each posture (standing, bowing, prostrating, sitting) during prayer.
قاعدہ اولی (qa'da ula): The first sitting after two rak'ats in a prayer of three or four rak'ats; it is wajib to sit briefly even if one does not recite tashahhud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the consequence of omitting a wajib in salah according to the Hanafi school?
A) The prayer becomes invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid but requires sajda sahw.
C) The prayer is valid and no compensation is needed.
D) The prayer is valid but must be repeated if omitting an obligatory act.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a wajib act in salah does not invalidate the prayer if omitted; compensation via sajda sahw suffices.

The Hanafi-Shafi'i Difference: Wajib vs Sunnah
Comparing the Hanafi and Shafi'i categorizations of certain prayer acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare the Hanafi concept of wajib with the Shafi'i classification and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Imam Shafi'i does not recognize a separate wajib category; acts deemed wajib by Hanafis are sunnah in the Shafi'i school.

The Hanafi school uniquely distinguishes between fard and wajib. Imam Shafi'i, however, holds that every commanded act is either obligatory (fard) or recommended (sunnah). This leads to differences in ruling on acts like tadelil arkan and qa'da ula.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on wajib
Wajib is an obligatory act whose omission does not invalidate prayer but requires sajda sahw.
Examples: tadelil arkan, qa'da ula.
2
State the Shafi'i position
According to the text, Imam Shafi'i says there is no wajib category; these acts are sunnah after fard.
Some Shafi'i sources consider tadelil arkan as fard, but the passage attributes sunnah to Imam Shafi'i.
3
Identify the specific examples from the text
The text mentions tadelil arkan and qa'da ula as wajib in Hanafi; in Shafi'i, they are considered sunnah.
This is directly from the last sentence of the passage.
4
Analyze the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
In Hanafi, omitting these acts requires sajda sahw; in Shafi'i, omitting a sunnah does not require any compensation.
Also, if one deliberately omits a sunnah, it is disliked but prayer is valid.
5
Understand the methodological basis
The difference stems from the definition of 'wajib' in usul al-fiqh and the Hanafi stance on ahad hadith as sufficient to establish obligation (wujub) but not at the level of fard.
This is not explicitly in the text but is background knowledge.

Source Text

ضروری نوٹ : واجب کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اس کو کرنا ضروری ہے، اور وہ چھوٹ گیا تو نماز فاسد نہیں ہوگی البتہ سجدہ سہو لازِم ہوگا، اور اگر سجدہ سہو بھی نہیں کیا تو کراہیت کے ساتھ نماز پوری ہوگئی ، بہتر یہ ہے کہ اس نماز کو دوبارہ پڑھ لے، اور نہیں پڑھی تب بھی فرض ادا ہو گیا۔ اس حدیث میں صحابی نے تعدیل ارکان نہیں کی جو واجب تھی تو دوبارہ نماز پڑھنے کے لئے فرمایا۔ عن ابی ھریرة عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم دخل المسجد فدخل رجل فصلى ثم جاء فسلم على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فرد النبي عليه السلام فقال: ارجع فصل فانك لم تصل .... ثم اركع حتى تطمئن راكعا ثم ارفع حتى تعتدل قائما ، ثم اسجد حتى تطمئن ساجدا ثم ارفع حتى تطمئن جالساً ، ثم اسجد حتى تطمئن ساجدا ، ثم افعل ذالک فی صلاتک کلها - ( بخاری شریف، باب امر النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم الذی لا یتم رکوعہ بالا عادة، ص ۱۲۸، نمبر۷۹۳رابوداود شریف ، باب صلوۃ من لا یتقیم صلبه فی الرکوع ولا السجود، ص۱۳۲، نمبر ۸۵۶) اس حدیث میں تعدیل ارکان جو واجب ہے اس کو چھوڑنے پر دوبارہ نماز پڑھنے کے لئے فرمایا۔ (۲) واجب کے بھولنے میں سجدہ سہو ہے ، اسکی دلیل یہ ہے۔ عن الـمـغيــرة بن شعبة قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اذا قام الامام في الركعتين فان ذكر قبل أن يستوى قائما فليجلس ، فان استوى قائما فلا يجلس و يسجد سجدتي السهو )) ۔ (ابوداود شریف ، باب من نسی آن يتشهد وهو جالس ، ص ۱۵۷ نمبر ۱۰۳۶ر ترمذی شریف ، باب ماجاء فی سجدتي السهو قبل السلام ، ص۹۰، نمبر ۳۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ قاعدہ اولی بھول جائے تو سجدہ سہو کرے، اور قاعدہ اولی واجب ہے جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ واجب کے چھوٹنے سے سجدہ سہو واجب ہوگا۔ امام شافعی کے یہاں واجب کا درجہ نہیں ہے، فرض کے بعد سنت کا درجہ ہے اس لئے انکے یہاں یہ سب سنت کے درجے میں ہیں ۔
Essential note: The meaning of wajib is that performing it is necessary, and if it is omitted, the prayer does not become invalid; however, sajda sahw becomes binding. And if sajda sahw is also not performed, then the prayer is complete with dislike. It is better to repeat this prayer, and if not repeated, still the obligation is fulfilled. In this hadith, the companion did not perform tadelil arkan which was wajib, so the Prophet commanded him to repeat the prayer. From Abu Huraira: A man entered the mosque and prayed, then came and greeted the Prophet. The Prophet replied: 'Go back and pray, for you have not prayed... then bow until you are at ease in bowing, then rise until you are standing straight, then prostrate until you are at ease in prostration, then rise until you are at ease in sitting, then prostrate until you are at ease in prostration, then do that in all your prayers.' (Bukhari, chapter on the command of the Prophet to the one who does not complete his bowing in the usual manner, p.128, no.793; Abu Dawud, chapter on the prayer of one whose back does not straighten in bowing and prostration, p.132, no.856) In this hadith, tadelil arkan which is wajib was omitted, so he was commanded to repeat the prayer. (2) For forgetting a wajib, there is sajda sahw; its evidence is: From al-Mughira ibn Shu'ba: The Messenger of Allah said: 'When the imam stands up after two rak'ats, if he remembers before fully standing, let him sit; if he fully stands, then do not sit and perform two prostrations of forgetfulness.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on one who forgets to sit for tashahhud, p.157, no.1036; Tirmidhi, chapter on what is related about sajda sahw before salām, p.90, no.39) In this hadith, if the first sitting (qa'da ula) is forgotten, then sajda sahw is performed, and qa'da ula is wajib, so it is known that omitting a wajib makes sajda sahw obligatory. According to Imam Shafi'i, there is no category of wajib; after fard comes sunnah, so with him all these are in the level of sunnah.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (ruling_with_proof). It begins by defining the legal category of 'wajib' in the Hanafi school: it is an obligatory act whose omission does not invalidate the prayer (salah) but requires compensation via sajda sahw (prostration of forgetfulness). If sajda sahw is also omitted, the prayer remains valid but is disliked (makruh), and repeating it is recommended. The passage then provides two hadith proofs. First is the famous hadith of the man who prayed hastily (the 'musalli' who did not perform tadelil arkan—the obligation to pause in each posture). The Prophet ordered him to repeat the prayer, showing that omission of a wajib (tadelil arkan) necessitates repetition. Second is the hadith of al-Mughira concerning forgetting the first sitting (qa'da ula). If the imam forgets and stands for the third rak'ah, he must perform sajda sahw. Since qa'da ula is wajib, this hadith establishes that omission of a wajib requires sajda sahw. Finally, the passage notes an inter-madhhab difference: Imam Shafi'i does not recognize the category of 'wajib' as distinct; he considers acts that are wajib in the Hanafi school as either fard or sunnah. This has practical implications for the number of obligatory elements in prayer according to each school.

Key Terms
واجب (wajib): An obligatory act whose omission does not invalidate the prayer but requires sajda sahw; it is a distinct category between fard and sunnah.
سجدہ سہو (sajda sahw): Two prostrations performed to compensate for forgetting a wajib or for making a mistake in prayer; they do not invalidate the prayer if omitted but their omission is disliked.
تعدیل ارکان (tadelil arkan): The obligation to pause and be at ease in each posture (standing, bowing, prostrating, sitting) during prayer.
قاعدہ اولی (qa'da ula): The first sitting after two rak'ats in a prayer of three or four rak'ats; it is wajib to sit briefly even if one does not recite tashahhud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) of the difference between Hanafi and Shafi'i regarding acts like tadelil arkan?
A) Hanafi requires sajda sahw; Shafi'i requires repeating the prayer.
B) Hanafi requires sajda sahw; Shafi'i does not require any compensation.
C) Hanafi does not require anything; Shafi'i requires sajda sahw.
D) Both require sajda sahw.

Key Takeaway
In the Shafi'i school, acts that are wajib in the Hanafi school are considered sunnah, so no sajda sahw is required for their omission.
