Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Reciting Surah al-Fatiha: A Wajib Act in Salah
Ruling determination with proofs: Fatiha is wajib, not fard.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reciting Surah al-Fatiha in salah, differentiate between fard and wajib using evidence, and compare the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on this issue.

Core Idea
A prayer without Fatiha is deficient, not invalid — the Hanafi wajib classification preserves its validity.

The status of Surah al-Fatiha in prayer is a point of scholarly debate. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position that it is wajib (necessary) rather than fard (obligatory), supported by Qur'an and hadith, and explains why the Shafi'i school differs. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the rules of sajda sahw and avoiding the misconception that every omission invalidates the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the Hanafi ruling
The act is reciting Surah al-Fatiha in salah. The Hanafi ruling is that it is wajib, not fard. 'Wajib' means necessary but not at the level of a pillar; its omission does not invalidate the prayer but requires sajda sahw.
Compare with 'fard' which invalidates the prayer if omitted.
2
Locate the primary evidence that any Quran recitation is fard
The first set of proofs (Qur'an 73:20 and hadiths) establish that reciting any portion of the Quran is fard. The imperative 'faqra'u' indicates obligation, and 'ma tayassara' shows that any easy part suffices. This proves Fatiha is not exclusively fard.
This is the Hanafi rebuttal to the Shafi'i claim that Fatiha itself is fard.
3
Analyze the hadiths specifically emphasizing Fatiha
Hadiths like 'la salata liman lam yaqra' bi-Fatihati al-kitab' and 'hiya khidaj' are used. The term 'khidaj' (deficiency) is key: the Hanafis interpret it as a deficiency that can be compensated by sajda sahw, not as a condition for validity.
The Shafi'is interpret the same hadiths as establishing Fatiha as a pillar (fard).
4
Understand the role of sajda sahw
Because the prayer is valid but deficient when Fatiha is omitted (deliberately or forgetfully), sajda sahw is prescribed to complete the prayer. This confirms the wajib status: omission of wajib triggers compensation, not repetition.
If it were fard, the prayer would be invalid and must be repeated.
5
Compare with the Shafi'i position and identify the practical difference
The Shafi'i school holds Fatiha is fard (a rukn). Therefore, if omitted deliberately, the prayer is batil (invalid); if forgotten, the rak'ah must be repeated. In the Hanafi school, the prayer remains valid and sajda sahw suffices.
This thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) directly affects the muqtadi and the imam.

( بخارى شريف، باب وجوب القراءة للامام والماموم في الصلوة كلها ص ۱۰۴ نمبر ۷۵۶ مسلم شریف ، باب وجوب قراءة الفاتحة في كل ركعته ،ص ۱۶۹، نمبر ۸۷۴/۳۹۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سورہ فاتحہ پڑھنا واجب ہے۔ نہیں پڑھیں گے تو کمی رہ جائے گی ۔ حدیث میں ہے (۲) عن ابي هريرة عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال من صلى صلوة لم يقرأ فيها بام القرآن فهى خداج ثلاثا غير تمام مسلم شریف، باب وجوب قراءة الفاتحة في كل ركعة ، ص ۱۶۹ نمبر ۱۷۸۷۸/۳۹۵ بو داؤد شریف، باب من ترک القراءة في صلوته، ص ۱۲۵، نمبر ۸۲۱) فهى خداج کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ فاتحہ چھوڑنے سے نماز میں کمی رہ جائے گی اور اس کا اتمام سجدہ سہو سے کرنا پڑے گا۔ اسی لئے حنفیہ کے یہاں سورہ فاتحہ پڑھنا واجب ہے ، اور چھوڑنے سے نماز ہو جائے گی لیکن سجدہ سہو کرنا ہوگا۔ ترجمه : (۳۹۱) [۲] فرض کی دورکعتوں میں سورت ملائے یا کم از کم تین آیتیں ملائے [۲] اور وتر کی (۳) اور نفل کی تمام رکعتوں میں سورت ملائے ۔ تشریح : [1] فرض کی پہلی دو رکعتوں میں یا دوسری دورکعتوں میں سورت ملانا واجب ہے، یا کم سے کم تین چھوٹی آیتیں، یا ایک
Chapter on the obligatory elements of prayer. (390) Recitation of al-Fatiha. (391) Adding a surah or three verses in two unspecified rak'ats of the obligatory prayer. And the summary: (390) [1] Reciting Surah al-Fatiha. Explanation: Reciting Surah al-Fatiha in prayer is not fard according to us but wajib. Evidence: (1) The evidence for the obligation of reciting the Quran from anywhere is this verse: 'Recite what is easy for you of the Quran' (73:20). (2) In the hadith: from Ibn Sa'id who said: 'We were commanded to recite the Fatiha of the Book and what is easy.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on one who abandons recitation in his prayer, p.125, no.818; Nasa'i, chapter on making recitation of Fatiha obligatory in prayer, p.105, no.1912) (3) In Bukhari: The Prophet said to the desert man who prayed hastily: 'Then recite what is easy for you of the Quran.' (Bukhari, chapter on the obligation of recitation for the imam and the follower in all prayers, p.105, no.757; Muslim, chapter on the obligation of reciting Fatiha in every rak'ah, p.170, no.885/397) This means that reciting what is easy of the Quran is fard, even if it is other than Surah Fatiha. (4) Abu Huraira reported: The Messenger of Allah said to me: 'Go out and proclaim in Medina that there is no prayer except with the Quran, even if it is the Fatiha of the Book or more.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on one who abandons recitation in his prayer, p.126, no.819) This hadith indicates that whether it is Surah Fatiha or another verse, the prayer is valid, which shows that reciting Fatiha is not fard; however we say it is wajib. Proof that Surah Fatiha is wajib: (1) From Ubada ibn al-Samit: The Messenger of Allah said: 'There is no prayer for the one who does not recite the Fatiha of the Book.' (Bukhari, no.756; Muslim, no.874/394) This hadith shows that reciting Surah Fatiha is wajib; if one does not recite it, there will be deficiency. (2) From Abu Huraira: The Prophet said: 'Whoever prays a prayer in which he does not recite the Umm al-Quran (Fatiha), it is deficient' – three times, not complete. (Muslim, no.878/395; Abu Dawud, no.821) 'Fa hiya khidaj' means that by omitting Fatiha, a deficiency remains in the prayer, and its completion must be made up by sajda sahw. Therefore, according to the Hanafis, reciting Surah Fatiha is wajib, and if omitted, the prayer is valid but sajda sahw must be performed. Translation: (391) [2] In the two rak'ats of the obligatory prayer, one should add a surah or at least three verses, and in witr and in all rak'ats of nafl, one should add a surah. Explanation: [1] In the first two rak'ats of the obligatory prayer or in the other two rak'ats, adding a surah is wajib, or at least three short verses, or one ...
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (ruling_with_proof) concerning the recitation of Surah al-Fatiha and an additional surah in the obligatory prayer. It first states the Hanafi position: reciting Surah Fatiha is wajib, not fard. It provides four proofs to establish that reciting any part of the Quran is fard (thus Fatiha is not exclusively fard), and then two specific proofs establishing the obligatory nature (wujub) of Fatiha itself. The four proofs are: (1) Quranic verse 'faqra'u ma tayassara min al-Quran' (Surah al-Muzzammil, 73:20), which indicates reciting any easy part is fard. (2) Hadith commanding to recite Fatiha and what is easy. (3) The Hadith of the man who prayed incorrectly, where the Prophet said 'then recite what is easy for you of the Quran,' implying that any part suffices for the fard requirement. (4) The Hadith that there is no prayer without Quran, even if only Fatiha, showing even Fatiha alone suffices (so it is not fard to recite only Fatiha). Then to prove that Fatiha itself is wajib, two hadiths are cited: (1) The hadith of Ubada: 'No prayer for one who does not recite Fatiha'; (2) The hadith that a prayer without Fatiha is deficient (khidaj). The term khidaj is interpreted as deficiency that is compensated by sajda sahw, confirming the Hanafi classification of wajib (not fard). The passage then moves to item (391): adding a surah (or at least three verses) in two specified rak'ats of the obligatory prayer, and in all rak'ats of witr and nafl. This is also wajib. The text cuts off during the explanation but the ruling is clear.

Key Terms
قرائة الفاتحة (qira'at al-fatiha): Recitation of Surah al-Fatiha in salah; it is wajib according to the Hanafi school.
سورة (surah): An additional surah (or three verses) recited after Fatiha in the first two rak'ats of obligatory prayer; its addition is wajib.
خداج (khidaj): Deficiency; a term used in a hadith to indicate that a prayer without Fatiha is incomplete, necessitating sajda sahw for completion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on reciting Surah al-Fatiha in the obligatory prayer?
A) It is fard (obligatory) and the prayer is invalid without it.
B) It is wajib and the prayer is valid without it but requires sajda sahw.
C) It is sunnah and optional.
D) It is only required for the imam, not the follower.

Key Takeaway
Reciting Surah al-Fatiha is wajib in Hanafi fiqh; its omission is compensated by sajda sahw, not by repeating the prayer.

Adding an Additional Surah in the Obligatory Prayer
Ruling on adding a surah or three verses in specified rak'ats.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adding a surah or three verses after Fatiha in salah, identify the required rak'ats, and explain the consequence of omission.

Core Idea
Joining an extra surah in the first two rak'ats of fard is wajib, completing the prayer's recitation structure.

In addition to reciting Surah al-Fatiha, the Hanafi school requires an additional surah (or at least three short verses) in specific rak'ats. This ruling applies to the first two rak'ats of obligatory prayers, as well as all rak'ats of witr and nafl. Understanding this helps ensure the prayer is performed with all its wajib elements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is adding an additional surah (or a minimum of three short verses) after reciting Surah al-Fatiha in prayer. The Hanafi ruling is that it is wajib in specific rak'ats.
This is separate from the wajib status of Fatiha itself.
2
Determine which rak'ats require the additional surah
The text states: in the first two rak'ats of the obligatory (fard) prayer, and in all rak'ats of witr and nafl prayers. The additional surah is not required in the last two rak'ats of a four-rak'ah fard prayer.
For a three-rak'ah witr, all three rak'ats require an additional surah.
3
Recognize the minimum amount of recitation
The minimum is three short verses or one long verse. The text mentions 'three verses' or 'one long verse' (the cut-off indicates 'one' possibly 'one long verse').
If no additional surah is added, the recitation is deficient.
4
Note the consequence of omission
Since it is wajib, forgetting to add the surah does not invalidate the prayer, but sajda sahw becomes wajib to compensate for the deficiency.
If deliberately omitted, the prayer is still valid but sinful.
5
Distinguish from other related rulings
For a follower (muqtadi) behind an imam, recitation of Fatiha and additional surah is not required; this ruling applies to the imam and the one praying alone. Also, for the third and fourth rak'ats of fard, only Fatiha is recited (some Hanafi scholars say tasbih is sufficient).
The source does not elaborate on this distinction, but it is important for practice.

فصل في واجبات الصلوة (۳۹۰) قرائة الفاتحة (۳۹۱) وضم السورة او ثلاث آيات فى ركعتين غير متعينتين من الفرض و جمه : (۳۹۰) [۱] سورہ فاتحہ پڑھنا۔ تشریح : نماز میں سورہ فاتحہ پڑھنا ہمارے یہاں فرض نہیں ہے بلکہ واجب ہے۔ وجه : (۱) کہیں سے بھی قرآن پڑھنے کی فرضیت کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ فاقرنوا ما تیسر من القرآن (آیت ۲۰ ،سورة المزمل ۷۳) (۲) حدیث میں ہے عن ابن سعید قال امرنا ان نقرء بفاتحة الكتاب وما تيسر ۔ (ابوداؤد شریف، باب من ترك القراءة (الفاتحة) فی صلوته بفاتحۃ الکتاب، ص ۱۲۵، نمبر ۸۱۸ / نسائی شریف ، باب ایجاب قراءة فاتحة الكتاب في الصلوۃ ص ۱۰۵ نمبر ۱۹۱۲ ) (۳) بخاری شریف میں ہے آپ نے اس دیہاتی سے فرمایا جس نے جلدی جلدی نماز پڑھی ثم اقرء ما تيسر معک من القرآن (بخاری شریف، باب وجوب القراءة للامام والماموم في الصلوة كلها ص ۱۰۵ نمبر ۷۵۷ رمسلم شریف ، باب وجوب قرائۃ الفاتحۃ فی کل رکعتۃ ص ۱۷۰ نمبر ۸۸۵/۳۹۷) اس کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ قرآن میں سے جو آسان ہو اس کا پڑھنا فرض ہے۔ چاہے سورہ فاتحہ کے علاوہ ہو۔ (۴) حدثنی ابو هريرة قال : قال لى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اخرج فناد في المدينة أنه لا صلوة الا بقرآن و لو بفاتحة الكتاب فما زاد ۔ (ابوداود شریف، باب من ترک القرآة في صلونة بفاتحة الكتاب ،ص ۱۲۶، نمبر ۸۱۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ سورہ فاتحہ ہو یا کوئی اور آیت ہو اس سے نماز ہو جائے گی جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ فاتحہ پڑھنا فرض نہیں ہے، البتہ واجب ہم بھی کہتے ہیں۔ سورة فاتحه واجب ھونے کی دليل: (۱) عن عبادة بن الصامت ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال لا صلوة لمن لم يقرأ بفاتحة الكتاب - ( بخارى شريف، باب وجوب القراءة للامام والماموم في الصلوة كلها ص ۱۰۴ نمبر ۷۵۶ مسلم شریف ، باب وجوب قراءة الفاتحة في كل ركعته ،ص ۱۶۹، نمبر ۸۷۴/۳۹۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سورہ فاتحہ پڑھنا واجب ہے۔ نہیں پڑھیں گے تو کمی رہ جائے گی ۔ حدیث میں ہے (۲) عن ابي هريرة عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال من صلى صلوة لم يقرأ فيها بام القرآن فهى خداج ثلاثا غير تمام مسلم شریف، باب وجوب قراءة الفاتحة في كل ركعة ، ص ۱۶۹ نمبر ۱۷۸۷۸/۳۹۵ بو داؤد شریف، باب من ترک القراءة في صلوته، ص ۱۲۵، نمبر ۸۲۱) فهى خداج کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ فاتحہ چھوڑنے سے نماز میں کمی رہ جائے گی اور اس کا اتمام سجدہ سہو سے کرنا پڑے گا۔ اسی لئے حنفیہ کے یہاں سورہ فاتحہ پڑھنا واجب ہے ، اور چھوڑنے سے نماز ہو جائے گی لیکن سجدہ سہو کرنا ہوگا۔ ترجمه : (۳۹۱) [۲] فرض کی دورکعتوں میں سورت ملائے یا کم از کم تین آیتیں ملائے [۲] اور وتر کی (۳) اور نفل کی تمام رکعتوں میں سورت ملائے ۔ تشریح : [1] فرض کی پہلی دو رکعتوں میں یا دوسری دورکعتوں میں سورت ملانا واجب ہے، یا کم سے کم تین چھوٹی آیتیں، یا ایک
Chapter on the obligatory elements of prayer. (390) Recitation of al-Fatiha. (391) Adding a surah or three verses in two unspecified rak'ats of the obligatory prayer. And the summary: (390) [1] Reciting Surah al-Fatiha. Explanation: Reciting Surah al-Fatiha in prayer is not fard according to us but wajib. Evidence: (1) The evidence for the obligation of reciting the Quran from anywhere is this verse: 'Recite what is easy for you of the Quran' (73:20). (2) In the hadith: from Ibn Sa'id who said: 'We were commanded to recite the Fatiha of the Book and what is easy.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on one who abandons recitation in his prayer, p.125, no.818; Nasa'i, chapter on making recitation of Fatiha obligatory in prayer, p.105, no.1912) (3) In Bukhari: The Prophet said to the desert man who prayed hastily: 'Then recite what is easy for you of the Quran.' (Bukhari, chapter on the obligation of recitation for the imam and the follower in all prayers, p.105, no.757; Muslim, chapter on the obligation of reciting Fatiha in every rak'ah, p.170, no.885/397) This means that reciting what is easy of the Quran is fard, even if it is other than Surah Fatiha. (4) Abu Huraira reported: The Messenger of Allah said to me: 'Go out and proclaim in Medina that there is no prayer except with the Quran, even if it is the Fatiha of the Book or more.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on one who abandons recitation in his prayer, p.126, no.819) This hadith indicates that whether it is Surah Fatiha or another verse, the prayer is valid, which shows that reciting Fatiha is not fard; however we say it is wajib. Proof that Surah Fatiha is wajib: (1) From Ubada ibn al-Samit: The Messenger of Allah said: 'There is no prayer for the one who does not recite the Fatiha of the Book.' (Bukhari, no.756; Muslim, no.874/394) This hadith shows that reciting Surah Fatiha is wajib; if one does not recite it, there will be deficiency. (2) From Abu Huraira: The Prophet said: 'Whoever prays a prayer in which he does not recite the Umm al-Quran (Fatiha), it is deficient' – three times, not complete. (Muslim, no.878/395; Abu Dawud, no.821) 'Fa hiya khidaj' means that by omitting Fatiha, a deficiency remains in the prayer, and its completion must be made up by sajda sahw. Therefore, according to the Hanafis, reciting Surah Fatiha is wajib, and if omitted, the prayer is valid but sajda sahw must be performed. Translation: (391) [2] In the two rak'ats of the obligatory prayer, one should add a surah or at least three verses, and in witr and in all rak'ats of nafl, one should add a surah. Explanation: [1] In the first two rak'ats of the obligatory prayer or in the other two rak'ats, adding a surah is wajib, or at least three short verses, or one ...
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (ruling_with_proof) concerning the recitation of Surah al-Fatiha and an additional surah in the obligatory prayer. It first states the Hanafi position: reciting Surah Fatiha is wajib, not fard. It provides four proofs to establish that reciting any part of the Quran is fard (thus Fatiha is not exclusively fard), and then two specific proofs establishing the obligatory nature (wujub) of Fatiha itself. The four proofs are: (1) Quranic verse 'faqra'u ma tayassara min al-Quran' (Surah al-Muzzammil, 73:20), which indicates reciting any easy part is fard. (2) Hadith commanding to recite Fatiha and what is easy. (3) The Hadith of the man who prayed incorrectly, where the Prophet said 'then recite what is easy for you of the Quran,' implying that any part suffices for the fard requirement. (4) The Hadith that there is no prayer without Quran, even if only Fatiha, showing even Fatiha alone suffices (so it is not fard to recite only Fatiha). Then to prove that Fatiha itself is wajib, two hadiths are cited: (1) The hadith of Ubada: 'No prayer for one who does not recite Fatiha'; (2) The hadith that a prayer without Fatiha is deficient (khidaj). The term khidaj is interpreted as deficiency that is compensated by sajda sahw, confirming the Hanafi classification of wajib (not fard). The passage then moves to item (391): adding a surah (or at least three verses) in two specified rak'ats of the obligatory prayer, and in all rak'ats of witr and nafl. This is also wajib. The text cuts off during the explanation but the ruling is clear.

Key Terms
ضم السورة (damm al-surah): Adding an additional surah after Surah al-Fatiha in salah; it is wajib in specified rak'ats.
آيات (ayat): Verses; the minimum for the additional recitation is three short verses or a long verse equivalent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, adding an additional surah after Fatiha is wajib in which of the following?
A) All rak'ats of all prayers.
B) First two rak'ats of fard and all rak'ats of witr and nafl.
C) Only the first rak'ah of every prayer.
D) Only in witr and nafl, not in fard.

Key Takeaway
Adding a surah or three verses after Fatiha is wajib in the first two rak'ats of fard and all rak'ats of witr and nafl; omission is compensated by sajda sahw.
